# Changelog

## MCP result completeness contract

- **Expose machine-readable result status.** `xray_grep`, `xray_definitions`, and `xray_callers` now return top-level `resultStatus` metadata describing completeness, exactness safety, evidence level, reasons, and collection accounting.
- **Report execution and scope decisions.** `xray_grep` includes top-level execution metadata, `xray_definitions` supports explicit exact-name and auto-correction controls, and `xray_callers` can mark production-only scope with node kinds.
- **Preserve result metadata during truncation.** Oversized responses now keep handler-specific `resultStatus` details such as definition requests, auto-correction data, and caller scope while marking the response as partial.

## MCP startup protocol observability

- **Trace MCP startup and tool discovery.** When `--debug-log` is enabled, the MCP stdio loop now records `PROTO` lifecycle events for `initialize`, `notifications/initialized`, `tools/list`, `tools/call`, and `ping` before handler dispatch, including roots capabilities and requested tool names.
- **Capture invalid protocol paths.** Malformed JSON, invalid request shapes, unsupported JSON-RPC versions, unknown message shapes, EOF, and shutdown reasons now appear in the protocol trace to distinguish host-side startup races from requests that reached xray.
- **Preserve stdout purity.** Protocol diagnostics are emitted only to stderr/debug logs, keeping stdout reserved for JSON-RPC responses.

## Language-aware xray guidance

- **Render guidance from active language capabilities.** MCP initialize instructions now distinguish content-indexed extensions from definition-parser extensions, so SQL, TypeScript/Angular, C#, Rust, and XML-on-demand guidance only appears when the corresponding runtime capability is available.
- **Guide known-symbol reads toward `xray_definitions`.** `xray_help` and initialize instructions now include an investigation decision tree and known-symbol shortcuts that prefer `xray_definitions includeBody=true` over raw file reads once a class, method, function, or stored procedure is known.
- **Make follow-up hints contextual.** Shared MCP response guidance now uses result paths, parser-active extensions, and invocation args to suggest scoped `xray_definitions` reads, SQL stored-procedure validation, and Angular selector parent lookups without overwriting handler-specific `nextStepHint` values.
- **Expose per-file readability metadata in `xray_info`.** File metadata now reports `definitionParserActive`, `xmlOnDemandActive`, and `symbolReadableViaDefinitions`, with hints for parser-backed source files and XML-on-demand files.
- **Clarify `xray_edit` tool choice.** `xray_help tool="xray_edit"` now includes a decision card for when to use `xray_edit` versus built-in whole-file writes.

## Debug-log startup diagnostics

- **Report debug-log initialization failures explicitly.** `xray serve --debug-log` now creates the `.debug.log` file before index build/load, reports filesystem failures to stderr with the target path and source error, and leaves debug logging disabled instead of claiming success when the file was not created.
- **Keep MCP startup best-effort for debug logging.** If the debug-log file cannot be created, the server continues normal MCP startup without polluting JSON-RPC stdout.

## SQL procedure/function signature parameters

- **Scope SQL signature params to declarations.** `xray_definitions` now builds stored procedure and function signatures from declaration headers only, preserving comma-leading and multiline params while excluding body locals and `EXEC` arguments.
- **Ignore comments and string defaults while detecting SQL headers.** Commented-out DDL no longer wins `CREATE` dispatch or signature starts, header comments do not add fake params, and defaults containing `--` or `/*` remain intact.
- **Harden inline and multiline signature formatting.** Inline typed params, CRLF headers, open-paren multiline functions, and partial first-line params no longer emit duplicate or malformed parameter lists.

## Guidance prefix for MCP responses

- **Add opt-in agent guidance prefix.** When `XRAY_GUIDANCE_PREFIX` is truthy, MCP tool responses move `summary.nextStepHint` and `summary.policyReminder` into a compact text prefix before the JSON payload, while default output remains JSON-only.
- **Apply prefix uniformly across all JSON-producing tools.** Prefix rendering covers every tool that injects guidance fields, including `xray_info`, `xray_help`, `xray_reindex`, and `xray_reindex_definitions`. Automation that consumes responses with `XRAY_GUIDANCE_PREFIX=1` must split the prefix from the JSON suffix before parsing.
- **Preserve response post-processing contracts.** Prefix rendering runs after guidance injection, unknown-argument warnings, metrics, and truncation, and recomputes final `responseBytes` and `estimatedTokens` for the actual response text.

## Angular context hints

- **Surface Angular navigation guidance in existing `summary.nextStepHint`.** `xray_definitions` now suggests selector-based parent lookups and class-based child lookups when component selector/template metadata is present, while `xray_callers` template-navigation responses clarify that nodes are component parents/children rather than method callers.
- **Preserve handler-specific MCP guidance.** Shared response guidance now keeps a handler-provided `nextStepHint` instead of replacing it with generic tool text.
- **Harden template-navigation follow-ups.** `xray_callers direction="up"` accepts known Angular selectors even when they do not contain `-`, and source hints resolve to repo-relative paths to avoid ambiguous basename-only `file=[...]` suggestions.

## Serve background build failure handling

- **Unblock startup waiters after detached index build failure or panic.**
  Background content/definition builds now mark a terminal build state when
  they fail or unwind, so the primary build lock and deferred git-cache rebuild
  do not wait forever on `*_building=true` with `*_ready=false`.
- **Keep `ready` reserved for usable indexes.** Failure and panic paths clear
  the building flag and mark terminal completion without setting
  `content_ready`/`def_ready`, preventing empty placeholder indexes from being
  served or persisted.

## Parallel trigram index build

- **Parallelize trigram index construction during cold build.** The trigram
  index (used for substring search) is now built using multiple threads via
  `std::thread::scope`. Tokens are split into chunks, each thread builds a
  local trigram map, and the results are merged. On large repos (3.8M tokens)
  this reduces trigram build time from ~8s to ~2-3s.
- Small indexes (<2000 tokens) use the serial path to avoid thread overhead.
- The same parallel path benefits `rebuild_trigram_index_singleflight` (lazy
  rebuild after watcher mutations).
- Deterministic output: tokens are sorted before chunking, and chunk indices
  are monotonically increasing, so merged posting lists remain sorted without
  an extra sort pass.

## Thread budget for serve cold start

- **Prevent oversubscription during cold start.** When `xray serve` needs to
  cold-build both content and definition indexes simultaneously, the combined
  worker thread count is now capped at `available_parallelism()` instead of
  each build independently taking the full core count (previously 2×N threads
  on an N-core machine).
- Default split: content build gets N/2 threads, definition build gets the
  remainder. Content walk is I/O-bound and benefits less from extra CPU;
  definition parsing is CPU-bound.
- Standalone CLI commands (`xray content-index --threads`, `xray def-index
  --threads`) are not affected — only the `serve` cold-start path.
- New env overrides for diagnostics: `XRAY_CONTENT_THREADS` and
  `XRAY_DEFINITION_THREADS` set explicit thread counts (≥1), bypassing the
  automatic split.
- New `threadBudget` phase in debug telemetry shows chosen thread counts,
  available parallelism, and env override status.
- 12 new unit tests for budget computation.


## 2026-04-28

### Diagnostics
- **lineRegex phase telemetry** — `xray_grep` now reports phase-level
  `summary.lineRegexScan` timings for candidate filtering, scope filtering,
  match bookkeeping, merge, sort/dedup, rank/truncate, response build,
  response finalization, and residual scan work. `perfHint` now names the
  measured bottleneck phase when phase telemetry is available.

### Performance
- **Autosave interval raised to 5 minutes** — prevents continuous autosave
  serialization on large repositories (>500 MB index) where a single
  autosave cycle exceeds the 30-second quiet interval. Reduces RwLock
  contention from ~70-80% to ~30-40% of active time. Trade-off: up to
  5 minutes of incremental index state may be lost on force-kill
  (recovered via 10-30s reconciliation on next startup).
- **Lock-free autosave serialization** — `periodic_autosave` now clones
  the index snapshot under a brief read lock (~1-2s) and serializes
  without any lock held. Previously, serialization of a 593 MB
  content-index held the read lock for 79-102 seconds, blocking all
  writers (edit sync-reindex, watcher batch, reconciliation) for the
  entire duration. Combined with the 30-second autosave interval, this
  caused near-continuous lock contention (~70-80% of active time) on
  large repositories. After this fix, read lock is held for ~1-2s
  regardless of index size. Peak memory increases by ~600 MB during
  autosave (snapshot lifetime).
- **Cross-thread autosave dirty flag** — `xray_edit` now signals the
  watcher thread when indexes are mutated via `reindex_paths_sync`.
  Prevents the watcher from clearing its `have_unsaved` flag when the
  just-saved snapshot is already stale from a concurrent edit.
- **Targeted content-index purge in watcher updates** — mutable watcher paths now
  maintain a derived per-file token reverse index (`file_id -> tokens`) so
  single-file edit/reindex purge touches only that file's token posting lists
  instead of scanning the entire inverted index. The reverse map is skipped on
  disk and rebuilt only for watch-mode mutation paths, while autosave snapshots
  deliberately omit it to avoid cloning hundreds of MB of derived state. Dirty
  files that fail retokenization now keep their old postings/counts until a later
  successful update, preserving index consistency.

### Performance
- **Skip trigram rebuild for narrow-scope grep** — after `xray_edit` sets
  `trigram_dirty=true`, scoped grep (`file=` or auto-phrase) no longer
  triggers a full trigram rebuild (~40-70s on large repos). Substring and
  lineRegex fall back to direct token/file scan when trigram is stale.
  Phrase: 43s→0.6s, lineRegex with `file=`: 68s→0.4s, memory stable.
- **Async trigram rebuild after `xray_edit`** — content-index updates now
  schedule trigram rebuild on a single-flight background thread. Wide
  trigram-dependent grep waits for an in-flight rebuild, while narrow grep
  keeps immediate correctness through the stale-safe direct scan path.

### Diagnostics
- **Sub-timing breakdown in `reindexElapsedMs`** — `xray_edit` response
  now includes `reindexDetail` with `tokenizeMs`, `contentLockWaitMs`,
  `contentUpdateMs`, `defLockWaitMs`, `defUpdateMs` for instant diagnosis
  of lock contention vs. actual reindex work.
- **`searchTimeMs` for `xray_edit`** — now reflects edit operation time
  (read + apply + diff + write + verify) instead of total wall-time
  including reindex. `totalTimeMs` remains the full dispatch-to-response
  time.
- **`xray_grep lineRegex` scan telemetry** — successful `lineRegex=true` summaries
  now include `lineRegexScan` with compile, literal-prefilter, scope-count, read,
  whole-file precheck, per-line evaluation, and scan-loop counters/timings for
  diagnosing wide-scope latency without changing search semantics.

## 2026-04-27

### Dispatch-level error pipeline — Phase 2 (BREAKING: dispatch gate errors now JSON-wrapped)

- **Refactor**: `dispatch_tool` split into `dispatch_tool` (3-line public wrapper) + `dispatch_inner` (all gate checks + handler dispatch) + `finalize_response` (guidance → unknown-args warning → metrics/truncation). `dispatch_inner` may `return` early from any gate — `finalize_response` always runs.
- **Fix**: 6 dispatch-level early-return sites (workspace unresolved/reindexing, content/def index not ready, `XRAY_STRICT_ARGS=1`, unknown tool) previously bypassed `inject_response_guidance` and `inject_metrics`. Now all gate errors carry `policyReminder`, `serverDir`, `workspaceStatus` (unconditional) and `totalTimeMs` (with `--metrics`). Plain-text gate errors are wrapped into `{"error": "...", "summary": {}}` by `inject_response_guidance`.
- **Bonus fix**: `truncate_response_if_needed` (utils.rs) now preserves `is_error` flag. Previously, truncation of oversized error responses silently flipped them to success (pre-existing bug, increased exposure from Phase 2 gate routing).
- **Tests**: 6 new tests in `handlers_tests_misc.rs` (4 gate-type coverage + metrics-off guidance + truncation `is_error` regression). Full suite: 2382 passed / 0 failed.


### MCP error responses — now JSON-wrapped + carry timing/policy metadata (BREAKING for raw text parsers)

Every **handler-level** error response from any xray MCP tool (`xray_grep`, `xray_edit`, `xray_definitions`, `xray_fast`, `xray_callers`, `xray_git_*`, ...) now flows through the same response pipeline as success responses: `inject_response_guidance` (wrap plain-text into JSON envelope + add `policyReminder` + workspace metadata) → `inject_metrics` (add `totalTimeMs` / `responseBytes` / `estimatedTokens` / `indexFiles` / `indexTokens`, **when `--metrics` is enabled**). The `policyReminder` and workspace metadata (`serverDir`, `workspaceStatus`) are injected unconditionally; `totalTimeMs` and other numeric counters require `--metrics` (the same flag that controls them on success responses).

- **Motivation**: a real-world 5–10 minute hang in `xray_edit` on a 140KB file was indistinguishable from "transport hang / dead pipe" because no timing reached the caller — the per-handler `ToolCallResult::error(plain_text)` skipped `inject_response_guidance` (not JSON), and `dispatch_tool` short-circuited on `is_error` before `inject_metrics`. Net effect: no `totalTimeMs`, no `policyReminder`, no `serverDir` on errors. Callers had no signal whether the server spent N ms on CPU or never received the request.
- **Fix — 3 small changes**:
  - [`inject_response_guidance`](src/mcp/handlers/utils.rs ): if the input text is not JSON AND `is_error == true`, wrap into `{"error": "<original-text>", "summary": {}}` so the rest of the pipeline can inject diagnostics. Plain-text **success** responses still pass through unchanged (no current tool emits them).
  - [`inject_metrics`](src/mcp/handlers/utils.rs ): preserve the `is_error` flag through JSON re-serialization (was always producing `ToolCallResult::success`).
  - [`dispatch_tool`](src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs ): removed the `if result.is_error { return result; }` short-circuit so metrics + response-size truncation run on errors too.
- **Caller-visible shape change** (BREAKING for one narrow class of clients):
  - Before: `result.content[0].text == "File 'X': Text not found: ..."` (plain string).
  - After: `result.content[0].text == r#"{"error":"File 'X': Text not found: ...","summary":{"totalTimeMs":591.4,"policyReminder":"...","serverDir":"...",...}}"#` (JSON envelope).
  - `is_error: true` at the MCP `ToolCallResult` layer is **preserved** — standard MCP clients (Claude Desktop, Claude Code, anything that checks `isError` first) are unaffected.
  - **At-risk**: custom tooling that does `text.contains(...)` / regex on the raw error string. Those need to either (a) check `isError` first then JSON-parse `text` and read `.error`, or (b) keep `text.contains(...)` style — the original error string is preserved verbatim under `.error`, so `text.contains("Text not found")` still works.
- **Out of scope** — 6 dispatch-level early returns (`Unknown tool: X`, `WORKSPACE_UNRESOLVED`, `WORKSPACE_REINDEXING`, `INDEX_BUILDING_MSG`, `DEF_INDEX_BUILDING_MSG`, `XRAY_STRICT_ARGS=1` violation) still bypass the pipeline (these are all sub-ms validation rejects where timing has no diagnostic value). Tracked separately in [`docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-27_dispatch-error-pipeline-bypass.md`](docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-27_dispatch-error-pipeline-bypass.md) (root cause analysis: `ToolCallResult::error` is a constructor not a pipeline stage; refactor proposals graded A/B/C).
- **Tests**: `test_metrics_not_injected_on_error` → `test_metrics_injected_on_error` (inverted contract). New per-tool error-path coverage: `test_metrics_injected_on_xray_edit_error`, `test_metrics_injected_on_xray_definitions_error`. All three assert `is_error` preserved + envelope parses + carries `totalTimeMs` + `policyReminder` + `serverDir`.

### `xray_edit` Phase 1 — error-feedback ergonomics & alias normalization

Implements items 1, 2, 5 (partial) and 6 of [`docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-26_xray-edit-error-feedback-and-swap-detection.md`](docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-26_xray-edit-error-feedback-and-swap-detection.md). Each change is purely additive on the response shape and behaviour; no schema break.

- **Silent alias normalization (AC-1b)**: `oldText` / `newText` / `oldString` / `newString` / `old_str` / `new_str` / `find` / `with` / `pattern` / `replacement` / `after` / `before` / `text` / etc. — every entry in `EDIT_FIELD_SYNONYMS` is now silently rewritten to its canonical name (`search`, `replace`, `insertAfter`, `insertBefore`, `content`, …) inside each `edits[]` item before validation runs. The previous "reject with hint" contract cost a round-trip on every cross-tool muscle-memory misfire (most common with agents trained on built-in `replace_string_in_file` style tools); silent acceptance turns those into successful edits while a real conflict (alias AND canonical present in the same item, e.g. `{ "search": "x", "oldText": "y", "replace": "z" }`) is still rejected with a precise diagnostic so user data is never silently dropped. Six previously-passing rejection tests in `edit_tests.rs` were flipped to assert silent acceptance.
- **Swap-or-already-applied hint (AC-1a)**: `Text not found` and `Pattern not found` errors now include a hint when the text the caller put in `replace` already appears verbatim in the file (length ≥ 8 chars to suppress noise on trivial substrings) — the textbook signal that either (a) `search` and `replace` are inverted, or (b) the edit was already applied in a previous batch. The hint also points the caller at `skipIfNotFound: true` for the idempotent-retry case. **Note**: the initial implementation used a fuzzy `find_nearest_match` scan (≥ 0.97 similarity) which added ~7s per failed edit on 100KB+ files; switched to O(N+L) `str::contains` after a real-world 15s stall on a 140KB edit. Near-miss cases (1–2 char drift) are still surfaced by the broader `nearest_match_hint` diagnostic on the same path, so no diagnostic surface is lost — only the targeted swap phrasing is suppressed in those edge cases.
- **Unified diff for structural mismatches (AC-2)**: when the nearest-match candidate has ≥ 3 lines, search text exceeds 80 bytes, and similarity is in `[0.80, 1.0)`, the hint now emits a 1-context-radius unified diff (capped at 20 lines) instead of the single-byte `First difference at byte N` marker. Backed by `similar::TextDiff::from_lines(...).unified_diff()` (`similar = "2"` already in `Cargo.toml`). Single-line, tiny, and exact-match cases keep the existing terser format — no regression on the 261-test pre-existing edit suite.
- **`editResults[]` always present (AC-5, partial)**: every successful edit response now carries `editResults: [{ "idx": <0-based>, "matchCount": <usize> }]` — one entry per input edit, in input order. Lets callers detect a single edit that hit more sites than intended (`occurrence: 0` over-match) without re-running the batch. Mode A line operations report `1` per successful op and `0` per skipped op; Mode B literal/regex/insert reports the actual replacement count (skipped via `skipIfNotFound` reports `0`). The `expectedMatches` enforcement half of AC-5 is deferred to a future Phase to keep this PR small.
- **Mixed-mode rejection (AC-6)**: was already implemented under [`check_unknown_edit_object_fields`](src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs ) — confirmed by the existing `test_edits_item_after_alias_*` family. Phase 1 documents the AC as already met.
- **Refactor**: extracted [`find_nearest_match`](src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs ) as a pure scan returning `Option<NearestMatch>`. After the substring-only swap detection switch, [`swap_or_already_applied_hint`](src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs ) no longer uses it; [`nearest_match_hint`](src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs ) and [`format_nearest_match_hint`](src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs ) remain as pure scan + pure formatter respectively. The dead alias → hint branch in [`check_unknown_edit_object_fields`](src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs ) was removed (aliases are now normalized BEFORE this validator runs). The `xray_edit` schema description in [`mod.rs`](src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs ) gained a `FIELD-NAME ALIASES` and `EDIT RESULTS` section.
- **Tests**: 13 new tests in `edit_tests.rs` (3 alias acceptance, 1 alias collision, 2 swap detection ± negative, 1 swap perf-regression guard on 70KB file, 1 swap min-length guard, 3 unified diff trigger ± boundary, 2 `editResults[]` shape & semantics). Full suite: 2373 passed / 0 failed (was 2363 / 0 — +10 net new + 6 rejection tests flipped in place to assert silent acceptance).
- **Out of scope for this PR** (Phase 2+): whitespace-tolerant auto-apply (story #4), batch `validateAll` mode (#3), `expectedMatches` enforcement (#5 second half), unified diff on the `Anchor text not found` path. Tracked in the same user-story.

## 2026-04-27

### Observability — `xray_grep` `lineRegex` `summary.literalPrefilter` scope-aware counters

- **New optional fields `totalFilesAfterScope` and `candidateFilesAfterScope`** in `summary.literalPrefilter`. Emitted only when the request carries any scope filter (`dir` / `file` / `ext` / `excludeDir` / `exclude`). Address the cognitive trap exposed during PR #222 cross-validation: a `dir`-scoped query and its unscoped sibling reported the **same** `candidateFiles` / `totalFiles` (because the trigram prefilter operates on the indexed corpus pre-scope, then `passes_file_filters` is applied per file inside the scan loop), masking the fact that scope had already done the heavy lifting and the prefilter was no longer the bottleneck. Now callers can compare `candidateFilesAfterScope` / `totalFilesAfterScope` to judge per-query selectivity.
- **`candidateFilesAfterScope`** is omitted when the prefilter did not produce a candidate set (`used: false`, e.g. ratio-guard short-circuit) — there is nothing to intersect with the scope.
- **Backward compatible**: existing fields (`used`, `candidateFiles`, `totalFiles`, `extractedFragments`, `reason`, `shortCircuited`, `extractedFragmentsTruncated`) keep their semantics; the JSON shape for unscoped queries is unchanged. Cost: one extra O(N) pass over `index.files` per scoped `lineRegex` call (microseconds even on 60k-file indices), gated by a single `params_have_scope_filter` check.
- **Tests**: 3 new integration tests in `handlers_tests_grep.rs` cover (a) `dir`-scope path with explicit candidate-vs-scope arithmetic, (b) `ext`-only scope path (the most common real-world shape), and (c) negative case asserting the new fields are omitted when no scope filter is set.
- **Documentation**: new "`literalPrefilter` scope-aware vs. global counters" subsection in `docs/mcp-guide.md` explains the pre-scope vs. post-scope distinction.

## 2026-04-26

### Reverted — `xray_grep` `lineRegex` alternation-split advisory (PR #222)

- **Reverted the advisory hint and the `summary.literalPrefilter.hasTopLevelAlternation` field added in PR #222.** Live cross-validation on a 66 743-file C# repo (2026-04-26) followed by a synthetic distributivity proof (`test_xray_grep_prefilter_distributive_over_top_level_or_pure_literal`, `test_xray_grep_prefilter_distributive_over_top_level_or_dotstar_blocked` in `handlers_tests_grep.rs`) showed that **the recommended `terms[]` split does not change the prefilter candidate set in our pipeline**. The advisory's central claim — *"splitting lets each branch be analysed independently, often yielding a much more selective fragment set"* — is false by construction: `compute_literal_prefilter` is **distributive over top-level OR**. For one term `"A|B"` the per-pattern path computes `posting(a) ∪ posting(b)`; for split `terms=["A","B"]` in OR mode the cross-pattern composition computes the same `posting(a) ∪ posting(b)`. Both forms yield identical `candidateFiles` and identical `extractedFragments`. The headline ~45× speedup originally cited came from a non-semantics-preserving rewrite (dropping `.*` from one branch), and the modest ~2.9× speedup from the genuine split traces to simpler per-line regex compilation, not to prefilter selectivity.
- **Detector retained**: `regex_has_top_level_alternation` in `grep_literal_extract.rs` (and its 11 unit tests) is preserved unchanged. It is a correct, low-cost building block that is likely to be useful for a future, properly-scoped advisory (see follow-up stories).
- **Distributivity tests added**: two new integration tests in `handlers_tests_grep.rs` build a synthetic content index, dispatch `xray_grep` with both forms (`["A|B"]` and `["A","B"]`), and assert `candidateFiles` and `extractedFragments` are equal. Lock-in protection: if the prefilter composition is ever refactored such that split *does* unlock new selectivity, these tests will fail and prompt re-evaluation of the advisory.
- **Follow-ups tracked outside the repo** (working notes): a per-line regex complexity advisory (the actual ~2.9× win observed in cross-validation came from per-line regex simplification, not from prefilter narrowing — a properly-scoped advisory would target *that* axis), and a scope-aware `literalPrefilter` counters proposal (when `dir=` / `file=` scopes a query, `candidateFiles` / `totalFiles` still report the **global** indexed-corpus counts, which is cognitively misleading).
- **Original story is left as-is**: `user-story_xray-grep-alternation-split-hint_2026-04-26.md` remains in the tree as a historical record of the spec that turned out to rest on a false premise; this CHANGELOG entry is the authoritative correction.

### Performance — `xray_grep` `lineRegex` literal-trigram prefilter (AC-4)

- **`xray_grep` `lineRegex` mode now extracts fixed-substring literals from each regex pattern via `regex-syntax` HIR `Extractor` and uses them as a trigram-prefilter pre-pass against the content index.** Files that cannot possibly contain any required literal are dropped before the per-file content read + per-line scan that previously dominated cold-cache cost (the user-story-cited 76 362 ms / 60k-file Shared-repo call set). Pure-substring searches still run through the existing trigram path with no change; the prefilter only kicks in on the `lineRegex=true regex=true` path that previously did a full corpus scan.
- **Eligibility**: per-pattern, only patterns whose AST exposes at least one literal of `MIN_LITERAL_LEN = 3` UTF-8 chars (Unicode-safe count, NOT bytes — important for Cyrillic / CJK identifiers). For OR composition (`mode='or'`) the prefilter unions candidate sets across patterns; for AND (`mode='and'`) it intersects. If any single OR pattern is unprefilterable (`\d+`, `.*`, `\w+`, `[a-z]+` etc.), the whole call falls back to no-prefilter (cannot soundly drop files for an OR'd unprefilterable branch).
- **Short-circuit guard**: if the candidate set still covers `> LITERAL_PREFILTER_MAX_RATIO = 50%` of the indexed corpus, the prefilter is discarded — the fixed cost of the trigram lookup + set-arithmetic outweighs the saved per-file work when most files survive anyway. Threshold chosen so the most degenerate case (universal trigram like `App` in a C# repo) gracefully degrades to today's behaviour with at most one extra <1ms trigram lookup added to the elapsed time.
- **Observability — new `summary.literalPrefilter` field** on every `lineRegex` response. Always emits `used`, `candidateFiles`, `totalFiles`, `extractedFragments` (the lowercased word fragments that were actually fed to the trigram lookup, **not** the raw `regex-syntax` literals — `"pub fn"` becomes `["pub"]` because `"fn"` is below the 3-char trigram floor). `extractedFragmentsTruncated` is added when there are more than 5 fragments. `shortCircuited` is added only when the ratio guard tripped. `reason` is added only when the prefilter did NOT run (or short-circuited) — it explains why (`"no pattern has extractable literals"`, `"OR mode contains an unprefilterable pattern"`, `"candidate set covers N/M files (>50% threshold)"`, etc.). Two example shapes:
  ```json
  // applied:
  "literalPrefilter": {
    "used": true,
    "candidateFiles": 142,
    "totalFiles": 60314,
    "extractedFragments": ["orgapptypeid", "apptype"]
  }
  // skipped (no extractable literal):
  "literalPrefilter": {
    "used": false,
    "candidateFiles": 0,
    "totalFiles": 60314,
    "extractedFragments": [],
    "reason": "no pattern has extractable literals"
  }
  ```
  The pre-existing `perfHint` copy is updated to acknowledge the prefilter when fired (`"... even with the literal-trigram prefilter applied ..."`) vs. not (`"... could not narrow the search ..."`). A structured `code` discriminator (so callers don't have to parse `reason` text) is intentionally deferred to a follow-up — the current `reason` string is best-effort prose, not API contract.
- **Differential test guarantees parity, not just speed**: `test_xray_grep_line_regex_prefilter_differential_parity` runs a 6-file fixture, dispatches the same `xray_grep` call twice — once with the prefilter, once with `set_line_regex_prefilter_disabled_for_test(true)` — normalises occurrences (basename + line numbers) and asserts equality. The toggle is `#[cfg(test)]`-only via thread-local `Cell<bool>`; the production path has no runtime branch.
- **Bench coverage**: `benches/search_benchmarks.rs` adds `bench_line_regex_literal_extraction` with 5 representative patterns (constant_name `App\s*=\s*\d+`, anchored_word `^\s*pub\s+fn\s+\w+`, or_alternation `OrgAppTypeId|AppType\d+`, unprefilterable `\d+`, long_or_chain) — measures the dominant primitive cost (regex-syntax HIR walk + literal extraction), which is the only new per-call work added on the production hot path. Existing trigram benchmarks in the same file already cover the candidate-set lookup side.
- **End-to-end measurement**: `scripts/measure-ac4-shared.ps1` replays the 3 canonical user-story calls (`OrgAppTypeId\s*=\s*\d+`, `App\s*=\s*[0-9]+`, `OrgApp.*TypeId|App.*TypeId\s*=\s*\d`) against any repo via MCP JSON-RPC, runs each call N times (default 3), drops the cold-cache run, reports the median of the warm runs together with `summary.searchTimeMs`, `totalFiles`, `literalPrefilter.used`, `candidateFiles`, and `perfHint` presence. Fails loudly if the response lacks `summary.literalPrefilter` (so a stale binary cannot be silently mis-measured). Compare two binaries (baseline `main` vs feature branch) by running once with each `-XrayBin` and diffing the medians; numbers belong in [docs/measurements/ac4-literal-extraction-bench.md](docs/measurements/ac4-literal-extraction-bench.md).
- **Files**: new `src/mcp/handlers/grep_literal_extract.rs` (~143 LOC) + `grep_literal_extract_tests.rs` (22 unit tests covering basic / multi-byte / OR/AND / unprefilterable / anchored / character-class / nested groups). Wired into `src/mcp/handlers/grep.rs` via `compute_literal_prefilter` + `apply_literal_prefilter_summary`. 4 integration tests in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests_grep.rs` cover OR-union, AND-intersect, short-circuit guard, and "summary field always present". `regex-syntax = "0.8"` added as an explicit dep (was already a transitive dep via `regex`).
- **Test delta**: `cargo test --bin xray grep` 275 / 275 passing; `cargo clippy --bin xray --tests` clean. Bench harness compiles via `cargo bench --bench search_benchmarks --no-run`.
- **Story**: [`user-story_xray-grep-lineRegex-perf-hints_2026-04-26.md`](user-story_xray-grep-lineRegex-perf-hints_2026-04-26.md) §AC-4. AC-1..AC-3 (perfHint copy & gating, lineRegex anchor CRLF fix, count-only summary) shipped 2026-04-25; AC-4 was deferred pending a measurable design.


## 2026-04-25

### Rename — `appendIdiom` → `appendRangeHint` in `xray_edit` response (2026-04-25)

- Renamed the `appendIdiom` response field to `appendRangeHint` for clarity. The field contains `{startLine, endLine}` for an INSERT-after-EOF follow-up call. Old name was confusing (`start > end` looked like a bug) and didn't convey its purpose.

### BREAKING (MCP single-string params: strict typing — step 2 of 2026-04-25 strict-typing migration)

- **Single-string MCP parameters now hard-reject wrong-type input (`array`, `number`, `bool`, `object`) and empty/whitespace-only strings.** Closes the asymmetry left over after the 2026-04-25 list-params migration: every list-shaped param (`terms`, `name`, `kind`, `file`, `parent`, `method`, `pattern`, `ext`) was strictified through `read_string_array`, but the matching single-value siblings (`class`, `attribute`, `baseType`, `from`, `to`, `date`, `author`, `message`, `path`, `repo`, `file` in git tools, `direction`, `mode`, `sortBy`) were still parsed by hand-rolled `args.get(K).and_then(|v| v.as_str())`. Wrong-type input on the OPTIONAL filter half (`class=["X"]`, `attribute=42`, etc.) silently dropped the filter and let the query proceed against the unfiltered superset — a real correctness regression, exhibited by [`scripts/test-r3-class-array.ps1`](scripts/test-r3-class-array.ps1) which produced a 21-node call tree from `xray_callers method=["dispatch_tool"] class=["OrderService"]` instead of an error. Wrong-type input on the REQUIRED half (`repo`, `file`) collapsed to a misleading `"Missing required parameter"` error. Empty strings (`baseType=""`, `class=""`) silently fell through to no-filter.
- **Migration recipe** for callers (LLMs, scripts, custom MCP clients):
  - single value: `"class": ["UserService"]` -> `"class": "UserService"`
  - empty (was `"baseType": ""`): omit the key entirely
  - enum: `"direction": ["up"]` -> `"direction": "up"`
- **Validator surface**: four new helpers in `src/mcp/handlers/utils.rs`, symmetric to the existing `read_string_array`:
  - `read_string(args, key) -> Result<Option<String>, String>` — optional. `Ok(None)` on missing/null; `Err` on wrong type, empty string, or whitespace-only string. Internal whitespace is preserved (regex-significant, mirror of `read_string_array` element-skip semantics).
  - `read_required_string(args, key) -> Result<String, String>` — required. Distinguishes `"Missing required parameter: '<key>'."` (missing/null) from the wrong-type message; the legacy pattern collapsed both into the misleading "missing" error.
  - `read_enum_string_with_default(args, key, allowed, default)` — closed-set + default. Used for `direction` (default `"up"`) and `mode` (default `"or"`). Case-insensitive membership, returns the user-supplied casing.
  - `read_enum_string_opt(args, key, allowed)` — closed-set, no default (returns `None` when absent). Used for `sortBy` where unset means "do not sort".
  Error messages cite the key in single quotes, name the offending JSON type, and reference the `2026-04-25` migration plus a usage example — mirror of the `read_string_array` diagnostic shape pinned in `read_string_array_rejects_string_form_with_actionable_message`.
- **Drift-guards for the bare-string enum domains.** `direction`, `mode`, `sortBy` are not backed by Rust enums (they are JSON strings), so the compile-time exhaustive-match guard used for `kind`/`ALL_KINDS` is not available. Three `pub(crate)` const slices were added next to their consumers — `ALL_DIRECTIONS = &["up","down"]` (in `callers.rs`), `ALL_GREP_MODES = &["or","and"]` (in `grep.rs`), `ALL_SORT_FIELDS = &["cyclomaticComplexity","cognitiveComplexity","maxNestingDepth","paramCount","returnCount","callCount","lambdaCount","lines"]` (in `definitions.rs`). Drift-guard tests in `src/mcp/handlers/utils_tests.rs::drift_guards` pin the slice contents AND assert that every entry in `ALL_SORT_FIELDS` round-trips through `read_enum_string_opt` while a non-member produces an error enumerating the full slice — if a developer adds a variant without wiring up the consumer (or vice versa), the test fires.
- **Tier-1 + Tier-2 in this PR; Tier-3 deferred.** The 24 sites where wrong-type input actually changes user-visible behaviour are migrated:
  - High-severity optional filters (silently-dropped before): `callers.rs::class` x1, `definitions.rs::{attribute, baseType}` x2, `git.rs::{from, to, date, author, message, path}` x14.
  - Medium-severity enum defaults (silently-coerced before): `callers.rs::direction` x2, `grep.rs::mode` x1, `definitions.rs::sortBy` x1.
  - REQUIRED params (`git.rs::{repo x5, file x2}`) also migrated to `read_required_string` because they share the helper and benefit from the wrong-type-vs-missing distinction.
  Deferred to a hypothetical step 3: `fast.rs::dir` x2, `mod.rs::dir` x2, `grep.rs::dir` x1, `edit.rs::path` x1 (all have a default-from-server-dir fallback that masks wrong-type as "user wanted default" — net win is error-message clarity only). Numeric/bool params (`maxResults`, `dryRun`, etc.) also out of scope.
- **CLI is unaffected.** All CLI subcommands continue to accept the same input shapes; the migration is exclusively at the MCP JSON-RPC boundary.
- **`xray_definitions` `sortBy` validation consolidated.** The inline `if let Some(ref sort_field) = sort_by { let valid = ["cyclomaticComplexity", ...]; if !valid.contains(&sort_field.as_str()) { return Err("Invalid sortBy value '...'") } }` block in `parse_definition_args` was deleted in favour of the single `read_enum_string_opt(args, "sortBy", ALL_SORT_FIELDS)?` call. Behaviour is preserved (same closed set of 8 valid values); the only user-visible change is the unified error shape `'sortBy' must be one of [...]` instead of the bespoke `Invalid sortBy value '...'`.
- **Test coverage delta**: full `cargo test --bin xray --features lang-csharp,lang-typescript,lang-rust` **2 293 passed** (was 2 264 pre-PR; +29 net new tests). Coverage focus: `read_string` happy-path/null/wrong-type/empty/whitespace; `read_required_string` missing-vs-wrong-type distinction; `read_enum_string_*` member/non-member/wrong-type/case-insensitivity; one e2e in [`e2e-test.ps1`](e2e-test.ps1) (`T-CLASS-ARRAY-REJECT`) asserting `class=["..."]` is hard-rejected with `isError=true` plus `'class'` and `2026-04-25` in the hint. In addition to the +29 new tests, 1 existing test was deleted (`test_base_type_empty_string_treated_as_no_filter` — its premise ("silent None") is now contradicted by the strict contract) and 2 were renamed/updated to assert the new behaviour (`test_parse_args_base_type_empty_string_is_none` → `_rejected`; `test_parse_args_sort_by_invalid_rejected` switched its assertion from `Invalid sortBy value 'X'` to `'sortBy' must be one of [...]`). `cargo clippy --tests --bin xray -- -D warnings` clean.
- **Provenance**: surfaced during Tier-3/Tier-5 cross-validation of the 2026-04-25 list-params migration (session 2026-04-25). Story [`docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-25_strict-string-params-step2.md`](docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-25_strict-string-params-step2.md) §8 documents the validation findings (real bug; inventory accurate; severity tiering; recommended scope cut to Tier-1+2 for first PR). Two cross-LLM-review adjustments from the validation pass were applied during implementation: (1) `read_string` returns `Err` on empty/whitespace (not `Ok(None)`) — silently treating empty as absent would re-introduce the same "silent filter dropped" failure mode the migration is closing; (2) drift-guard tests are direct unit tests on the helpers + const slices, not live JSON-RPC dispatch — the e2e dispatch surface is already covered by [`scripts/test-r3-class-array.ps1`](scripts/test-r3-class-array.ps1).


### UX (xray_definitions XML on-demand: partial-path resolution — 2026-04-25)

- **`xray_definitions` XML on-demand now resolves basename / path-suffix inputs against the indexed file list when the verbatim path does not exist on disk.** Previously, `file=["app.config"] name=["X"]` failed with `"Failed to resolve XML file 'app.config': ..."` even when exactly one indexed XML file ended in `app.config` — callers were forced to round-trip through `xray_fast` to discover the canonical path before re-issuing `xray_definitions`. After this change, the unique indexed match is silently re-resolved through the same `resolve_xml_file_path` sandbox check, so basename and path-suffix inputs (e.g. `configs/app.config`) work transparently without weakening the workspace boundary.
- **The fallback uses path-component-aligned suffix matching, not substring.** The 2026-04-17 security review explicitly forbade `web.config` resolving to `webapp.config` (different basename component, but a substring match would silently leak data from the wrong file). The new `resolve_via_index_suffix` helper splits both input and indexed paths on `/` (after `\\` → `/` normalisation), then requires the **last N components** of the indexed path to be byte-equal (case-insensitive) to the input components. `web.config` therefore does NOT match `site/webapp.config` because the basenames differ — the existing `test_xml_resolve_no_substring_collision` regression test stays green.
- **Ambiguity is reported, never silently merged.** When two or more indexed files end with the same path-component suffix, the handler returns an error listing up to 5 candidates plus the array-form `xray_fast pattern=["..."]` remediation hint. No silent pick, no merge across files. (`xray_fast` requires array `pattern` post-2026-04-25 list-params migration; the hint reflects that.)
- **Sandbox contract preserved (MAJOR-2 from the 2026-04-17 review).** The fallback is **gated to plain workspace-relative inputs**: absolute paths (`/etc/app.config`, `C:\\etc\\app.config`), Windows drive prefixes, and inputs containing `..` segments fall through to the original `resolve_xml_file_path` error unchanged. Without this gate, an explicit outside-workspace input could be silently reinterpreted as a suffix query against an unrelated indexed file with the same trailing components — downgrading the explicit-rejection contract to "reinterpret if it happens to match". Caught by the commit-reviewer subagent in the first iteration of this fix.
- **Performance: zero regression on exact-path requests.** The suffix lookup runs ONLY on the not-found error path. The matcher is `O(F * C)` where `F = indexed_files.len()` and `C = input.components().len()` — a linear scan over file paths with a short component-equality check per file, well below the cost of the canonicalisation that just failed.
- **Internal mechanism**: `try_intercept` in `src/mcp/handlers/xml_on_demand.rs` gained an `indexed_files: &[String]` parameter, threaded from `&index.files` at the single call site in `handle_xray_definitions`. New `pub(crate) enum SuffixResolution { Unique(String), Ambiguous(Vec<String>), None }` and `pub(crate) fn resolve_via_index_suffix(input, indexed_files) -> SuffixResolution` encapsulate the matching logic and are unit-testable without filesystem fixtures.
- **Provenance**: surfaced during the 2026-04-25 LLM-agent cross-repo session that produced `docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-25_definitions-file-suffix-matching.md`. The original story complained about silent zero-results for `file=["Foo.cs"]`, but code validation showed the index-based path already does substring resolution via `apply_entry_filters` — the real gap was the XML on-demand branch's exact-path requirement, narrowed and addressed here. Story §6 documents the validation findings and the closed acceptance criteria.
- **Tests** (`src/mcp/handlers/definitions_tests.rs`):
  - 4 integration tests via `handle_xray_definitions`: basename resolves to unique nested file; path-suffix (`configs/app.config`) resolves; ambiguous basename returns error with array-form hint; `web.config` does NOT resolve to `webapp.config` (security regression mirror).
  - 2 sandbox regression tests: absolute outside-workspace input (Unix `/etc/...` or Windows `C:\\etc\\...`) does NOT use fallback even when the trailing components match an in-workspace indexed file; `..` segments do NOT use fallback.
  - 8 unit tests on `resolve_via_index_suffix`: basename-unique, path-suffix-unique, ambiguous-lists-all, no-substring-collision, case-insensitive, normalises-backslashes, empty-input-is-none, input-longer-than-path-is-none.
  - All `#[cfg(feature = "lang-xml")]`. Full bin suite **2267 / 2267 passing**, clippy `-D warnings --all-features` clean. Reviewed by `commit-reviewer` subagent twice; both rounds caught real issues (sandbox-contract regression in absolute-path branch + stale single-quoted `xray_fast` hint shape) addressed before commit.


### Tooling (xray_info per-file metadata mode + xray_edit insert-idiom hint + xray_grep lineRegex CRLF anchor fix — 2026-04-25)

- **`xray_info` now accepts `file=["path", …]` and returns per-file metadata WITHOUT loading file contents into the response.** Closes the policy-violation escape hatch where agents fell back to `Get-Content | Measure-Object` (or `wc -l`) to discover line counts before composing an `xray_edit` call. Response shape: `{files: [{path, resolvedPath, lineCount, byteSize, extension, indexed, lineEnding}], summary: {requested, returned}}`. `lineCount` mirrors `edit::count_lines` exactly (trailing `\n` is a terminator, not a line) so the value can be fed straight back into `xray_edit` ranges — e.g. the append-EOF idiom `startLine: lineCount+1, endLine: lineCount`. Per-file errors (missing path, outside workspace, file > `MAX_INDEX_FILE_BYTES`) are reported in-band as `{path, resolvedPath, error}` so a single bad path in a batched request never aborts the rest. Workspace-boundary check uses `is_path_within` against BOTH raw `server_dir` and the canonicalised form (handles symlinks consistently with the rest of the path-security surface). `file=[]` (empty array) preserves the existing index-summary path — no shape change for the no-arg call. Schema published via `tools/list` declares `file` as `array<string>` and is automatically picked up by `arg_validation::known_args()` (no separate validator wiring).
- **`xray_edit` schema now teaches both insert-mode forms.** The `startLine` description spells out the append-EOF idiom (`startLine = lineCount+1, endLine = lineCount`); the `endLine` description (already shipped) documents the insert-before-line idiom (`endLine = startLine-1`). The `tips.rs` INTENT → TOOL MAPPING gets one new line `"INSERT lines (no replace)" -> xray_edit Mode A empty range: startLine:N,endLine:N-1 | startLine:lineCount+1,endLine:lineCount` so agents stop sending `startLine:N, endLine:N` (= REPLACE line N) when they meant to INSERT. Lock-in test `test_xray_edit_schema_teaches_insert_and_append_idioms` (`src/tips_tests.rs`) prevents regression of either schema string.
- **`xray_grep lineRegex=true` no longer silently misses anchored matches on Windows-edited (CRLF) files.** Root cause: `handle_line_regex_search` ran a fast-rejection pre-check `re.is_match(&content)` on whole-file content with `RegexBuilder::multi_line(true)` only. Under `multi_line` alone, `$` anchors before `\n` exclusively — on CRLF input the byte preceding `\n` is `\r`, so `\}$` against `}\r\n…` fails the whole-file pre-check and the file is dropped before per-line scanning ever runs. Symptom in transcripts: `xray_grep terms=["\}$"] lineRegex=true` returned 0 hits where `Select-String -Pattern '\}$'` returned thousands. **Fix**: add `.crlf(true)` to the `RegexBuilder` chain so `^` and `$` treat `\r\n` as a single line terminator, matching the `str::lines()` semantics already used by the per-line scan. `^`-anchored patterns were not affected (the per-line scan strips trailing `\r`, and `^` matches at every `\n`-bounded position regardless), so this is a `$`-anchor-on-CRLF-only fix — pure-LF behaviour is byte-identical to before. Schema description for `lineRegex` and the corresponding tip text both updated to spell out the new `crlf=true` contract, default case-sensitivity, and the `(?i)` opt-in.
- **UTF-16 line-ending detection (reviewer-caught MEDIUM, same change).** Initial `detect_line_ending` helper for the new `xray_info` file mode scanned at byte granularity — it correctly classified UTF-8 CRLF/LF/MIXED but misclassified UTF-16 LE/BE CRLF as `LF` because the on-disk byte preceding `0x0A` in UTF-16 is `0x00`, not `0x0D`. **Fix**: `detect_line_ending` now BOM-detects UTF-16 LE (`FF FE`) and UTF-16 BE (`FE FF`) and dispatches to a new helper `detect_line_ending_utf16(body, big_endian)` that scans at u16-code-unit granularity. The non-UTF-16 byte path is unchanged. Two regression tests in `handlers_tests_misc.rs` (`test_xray_info_file_mode_detects_crlf_in_utf16le_with_bom`, `..._utf16be_with_bom`) write BOM-prefixed UTF-16 files containing `a\r\nb\r\n` and assert `lineEnding == "CRLF"`.
- **Visibility wiring**: `tips.rs` fallback line in INTENT → TOOL MAPPING now reads `"If uncertain about file type/lines/encoding, call xray_info first (file=[\"X\"] -> lineCount/byteSize/lineEnding; not Get-Content/wc -l). Do not default to raw file reading."` — makes the new mode discoverable to LLM agents at tool-discovery time without bloating the instructions token budget (still under the 2250 ceiling enforced by `test_instructions_token_budget`).
- **Tests**: full bin suite **2253 / 2253 passing** (= 2244 pre-PR + 3 lineRegex CRLF + 9 xray_info file-mode + 1 schema lock-in − 0 deletions). Reviewed by `commit-reviewer` subagent twice; one MEDIUM finding (UTF-16 misclassification) addressed before commit. Bridge with the existing `appendIdiom` work in PR #212: the latter teaches the agent what to send next from a successful `xray_edit` response; this PR teaches it where to look BEFORE the first `xray_edit` call (file metadata, schema-level idiom hints) so the bursty-edit-followed-by-out-of-range cycle is broken at both ends.
- **Provenance**: surfaced during the 2026-04-25 LLM-agent debugging session that produced `docs/user-stories/todo_2026-04-25_xray-edit-append-and-line-staleness.md` §2.2 (CRLF anchor bug) and §2.3 (per-file metadata mode), plus a follow-up insert-idiom hint discussed mid-session. Closes both items + the open question §5.2 ("should `xray_info file` accept an array? — YES").



### BREAKING follow-up (file_filter_raw multi-file reject — 2026-04-25)

- **`xray_definitions` now hard-rejects multi-file `file=[A,B,...]` requests in two single-file-only code paths**: XML on-demand parsing (when the request shape is on-demand-eligible — has `name` or `containsLine` AND at least one entry has an XML-family extension) and `containsLine` substring lookup. Both paths are conceptually single-file (open one document; locate one line in one document) and previously degraded silently when given a multi-file array because the array was joined to a comma-string bridge (`"a.xml,b.xml"`) before reaching them. Symptoms before the fix: `file=["A.config","B.config"]` produced a cryptic "file not found" after a slow `fs::metadata` stat (XML on-demand tried to open the literal joined path); `file=["A.cs","B.cs"], containsLine=10` silently returned an empty result set (substring scan against the bridge string never matched any indexed file path).
- **Reject is gated on on-demand-eligibility, NOT on "array contains XML extension"**: requests that pass an XML-looking multi-file array WITHOUT `name`/`containsLine` (e.g. `file=["foo.xml","bar.xml"]` with no other filter) FALL THROUGH to the index path so its existing Hint E ("XML extension not indexed; use `containsLine` or `name`") can fire. Without this gate, the multi-file reject would preempt Hint E and suggest `file=["foo.xml"]` — but a one-element XML array without name/containsLine STILL would not activate on-demand parsing, so the suggestion would lead nowhere. (Caught by the commit-reviewer subagent in the first iteration of this fix.)
- **New error shape** (single-file-required diagnostic, raised before any filesystem access):
  - XML on-demand: `"XML on-demand requires a single file path, but `file` has 2 entries: [\"A.cs\",\"B.xml\"]. Run xray_definitions once per file (suggested first call: file=[\"B.xml\"]). XML on-demand opens and parses one file at a time; multi-file batching is not supported."` — the suggestion always points at the FIRST XML-looking entry in the array (B.xml in mixed-extension example), not at literal index 0.
  - `containsLine`: `"containsLine requires a single file in 'file' (got 2 entries: [\"A.cs\",\"B.cs\"]). Run xray_definitions once per file: file=[\"A.cs\"], containsLine=10."`
- **Internal mechanism**: a new `pub file_filter_raw: Vec<String>` field on `DefinitionSearchArgs` carries the un-normalized array straight from `read_string_array` (no lowercasing, no `\` → `/` rewrite). The legacy `file_filter: Option<String>` (comma-joined bridge) and `file_filter_terms: Option<Vec<String>>` (lowercased, slash-normalized for index-side substring matching) are retained for the hint paths and `file_matches_filter` that already split internally. The case-preserving `file_filter_raw` is mandatory for filesystem-touching code paths because case-sensitive filesystems (Linux/macOS) reject the lowercased path.
- **Provenance**: surfaced during cross-repo Tier 4.6 validation of the 2026-04-25 list-params migration in a C#/SQL/XML repository. The user observation `file=["Directory.Build.props","NuGet.Config"]` produced a cryptic single-file error, which led to the audit of all seven `args.file_filter` consumer sites and the severity classification (2 Important, 2 Low UX, 3 OK because they already split the joined bridge string internally).
- **Single-file array unaffected**: `file=["only.xml"]` (one element) continues to hit XML on-demand and `containsLine` exactly as before. The reject is keyed on `len > 1`, not on "is array".
- **Tests** (`src/mcp/handlers/definitions_tests.rs`):
  - `test_parse_args_populates_file_filter_raw` — pins the bridge-vs-raw contract.
  - `test_parse_args_file_filter_raw_empty_when_no_filter` — empty-when-absent invariant.
  - `test_parse_args_file_filter_raw_preserves_case` — critical regression guard for case-sensitive FS.
  - `test_contains_line_rejects_multi_file_array` — multi-file containsLine errors with `'single file'` + both filenames + `containsLine=N` echoed for actionability.
  - `test_contains_line_single_file_array_still_works` — single-element array still returns the containing class (regression guard so the new reject does not shadow legitimate calls).
  - `test_xml_on_demand_rejects_multi_file_array` — multi-file XML errors before any filesystem touch.
  - `test_xml_on_demand_single_file_array_still_works` — single-element XML on-demand still hits the XML parser (`summary.xmlOnDemand == true`).
  - `test_xml_on_demand_rejects_mixed_extensions_with_xml` — `file=["A.cs","B.xml"]` with `name` set rejects, echoes both filenames, and the suggested retry points at the XML-looking entry (`B.xml`) — not at the literal first slot.
  - `test_xml_on_demand_mixed_ext_falls_through_when_not_eligible` — `file=["A.cs","B.xml"]` WITHOUT `name`/`containsLine` does NOT error (the multi-file reject is gated on the on-demand-eligibility check, not on "array contains XML"). Pins the regression that the commit-reviewer subagent caught in the first iteration of this fix.
  - `test_hint_e_comma_separated_file_filter_with_name_rejects` — split from the previous `test_hint_e_comma_separated_file_filter`. Asserts the new error contract for the on-demand-eligible shape (multi-XML + `name`).
  - `test_hint_e_comma_separated_file_filter_without_name_falls_through_to_hint` — split from the previous `test_hint_e_comma_separated_file_filter`. Restores hint-path coverage for the file-only multi-XML shape (no `name`, no `containsLine`) — the multi-file reject must NOT preempt Hint E here.
- Full suite: **2 227 unit tests pass** (was 2 222 in the bin target before this follow-up; +5 net = 9 new tests added, 1 pre-existing test split into 2). All previously-passing tests still pass; only the renamed/split `test_hint_e_comma_separated_file_filter_*` pair changes contract from "asserts hint" to two distinct assertions tied to the new eligibility-gated reject.


### BREAKING (MCP list params: comma-strings → arrays — 2026-04-25)

- **MCP list-style parameters now require JSON arrays. Comma-separated strings are hard-rejected** with an error citing the param name, the date `2026-04-25`, and the word `array`. The migration covers every list-shaped MCP arg across the indexable surface:
  - `xray_grep`: `terms`, `file`, `ext`
  - `xray_definitions`: `name`, `kind`, `file`, `parent`
  - `xray_callers`: `method`, `ext`
  - `xray_fast`: `pattern`, `ext`
  - `xray_reindex`, `xray_reindex_definitions`: `ext`
  Single-string parameters were **not** touched: `class`, `dir`, `repo`, `path`, `xray_git_*.file` (single-file by design — `git --follow` semantics require one starting path).
- **Migration recipe** for callers (LLMs, scripts, custom MCP clients):
  - single value: `"terms": "foo"` → `"terms": ["foo"]`
  - multi-value: `"ext": "rs,toml"` → `"ext": ["rs", "toml"]` (note: split on commas — do NOT keep them inside a single element)
  - empty (was `"ext": ""`): `"ext": []` (or omit the key)
- **Why now**: the prior comma-string contract had two real defects. (a) Stringified arrays from JSON.stringify() — common when a caller naively passed a JS array to an MCP transport that didn't validate — became literal substring queries (`[\"foo\"]` searched for the bracket characters); auto-switch to phrase mode then masked the mistake with a misleading `searchModeNote`. (b) Values containing literal commas (path fragments, regex alternation) had to be escaped or carried in `phrase=true`. Closed-form arrays remove both ambiguity surfaces.
- **Validator surface**: a new helper `read_string_array` in `src/mcp/handlers/utils.rs` accepts JSON `array<string>` (and treats missing/`null` as the empty array), rejects every other shape — bare strings, numbers, objects, booleans — with the message `"'{key}' must be an array of strings (got {type}). The string-with-comma form was removed in the 2026-04-25 migration. Example: '{key}': ["a","b"]."`, and on a non-string array element returns the element-specific variant `"'{key}' must be an array of strings; element [{i}] is {type} (got {value}). Example: '{key}': ["a","b"]."`. Each handler dispatches through this helper at the boundary; downstream code paths that historically used `String + .split(',')` either consume the array directly (`xray_grep.terms`, `xray_callers.method`, `xray_fast.ext`) or take a `.join(",")` bridge for backward-compatible call sites (`xray_definitions.{name,kind,file,parent}`, `xray_callers.ext`, `xray_fast.pattern`, `xray_reindex(_definitions).ext`).
- **Drift-guard**: a new constant `ALL_KINDS: &[DefinitionKind]` next to the enum + an exhaustive-match unit test prevents the `kind` value list from drifting away from the source-of-truth enum (the previous schema-description list lagged the real enum by one variant — `xmlElement`).
- **CLI is unaffected**. `xray serve --ext rs,md` and all other CLI subcommands continue to accept comma-separated values; the migration is exclusively at the MCP JSON-RPC boundary. CLI users see no behavior change.
- **Tests**: helper-level coverage in `src/mcp/handlers/utils_tests.rs::read_string_array_rejects_string_form_with_actionable_message` pins the canonical rejection shape for the helper. Dispatcher-level coverage is split: a new table-driven test `test_all_migrated_keys_reject_bare_string_form` (in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests_misc.rs`) exercises 9 `(tool, key)` pairs from steps 2–4 (`xray_grep.{terms,file,ext}`, `xray_definitions.{name,kind,file,parent}`, `xray_callers.{method,ext}`) via the actual `tools/call` dispatcher — a future regression that re-introduces bare-string parsing in any of these handlers hard-fails; `xray_fast.{pattern,ext}` and `xray_reindex(_definitions).ext` are covered by per-handler regression-pair tests inline in their own test modules (added in steps 5/6). Positive-side regression tests assert array-form succeeds with discriminating output assertions (e.g., `files >= 1` for `ext=["rs"]` against a default `--ext cs` server, where bridge regressions would silently yield 0). End-to-end (`e2e-test.ps1`) rewrote 20 surviving string-form payloads to array form across xray_definitions, xray_grep, and xray_fast; full e2e suite passes 92/0.
- **Schema/`tools/list`**: the input schemas published via `tools/list` now declare these fields as `{"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}`. MCP clients that introspect the schema and validate before dispatch will surface the change at request time rather than as a runtime error.



### Reliability (PR-B: quiet-interval autosave — close the bursty-edit data-loss window)

- **`start_watcher`'s autosave gate is now two-tier: `AUTOSAVE_QUIET_INTERVAL` (30s) flushes after a recent burst, `AUTOSAVE_MAX_INTERVAL` (10 min, the legacy value, renamed for clarity) is the unconditional ceiling.** Closes Hole #2 from `user-stories/meta-checkpoint-durability.md`. Pre-PR-B the only autosave gate was `last_autosave.elapsed() >= AUTOSAVE_INTERVAL` (10 min). A user could delete 50 files (events processed by `process_batch`, in-RAM index updated), be idle for 9m59s, and force-kill the process — losing the entire 50-file delta because `periodic_autosave` had not yet fired. PR-A (post-reconcile checkpoint) didn't help because reconciliation only runs at startup, not on subsequent watcher events. PR-B adds a `have_unsaved: bool` flag set after every successful `process_batch` and cleared after every save; the new gate `autosave_due(have_unsaved, since_last_save)` returns `(have_unsaved && since_last_save >= AUTOSAVE_QUIET_INTERVAL) || since_last_save >= AUTOSAVE_MAX_INTERVAL`. Bounded data loss is now ~30s of unflushed activity instead of up to ~10 min.
- **Why this design**: bound expressed in seconds (user-meaningful) rather than in events (`notify` emits multiple events per file save — an event-count threshold is ambiguous). Single `bool`, not a counter — no `process_batch` signature change. Idle workspaces still write at most once per 10 min (`have_unsaved` stays false). Bursty workspaces write at most once per 30s of activity instead of unbounded amplification — the trade-off the user-story analyzed in detail.
- **Where the gate fires**: all three existing autosave check sites in `start_watcher` (force-flush after `MAX_ACCUMULATE`, idle-timeout in the empty-pending branch, opportunistic post-batch in the non-empty branch). The `have_unsaved=true` write happens immediately after each `process_batch` returns success on a non-empty input — by definition the in-RAM index has changes that haven't hit disk yet. Cleared after every successful save so the next 30s window starts fresh.
- **Helper extracted for testability**: `autosave_due(have_unsaved: bool, since_last_save: Duration) -> bool` is a pure function with no `Instant` / no I/O. Constants `AUTOSAVE_QUIET_INTERVAL` and `AUTOSAVE_MAX_INTERVAL` are `pub(crate)` so test code can reference them without hard-coded duplicates.
- **Tests**: `src/mcp/watcher_tests.rs` adds 5 unit tests:
  - `test_autosave_due_skipped_when_idle_and_below_max` — 0/29/120s and `MAX-1s` with `have_unsaved=false` all return false (steady-state idle).
  - `test_autosave_due_skipped_when_unsaved_but_below_quiet` — 0/15s and `QUIET-1s` with `have_unsaved=true` return false (avoids per-event amplification during a sustained burst).
  - `test_autosave_due_fires_on_quiet_interval_with_unsaved` — `QUIET`, `QUIET+1s`, 120s with `have_unsaved=true` all return true (the bursty-then-idle case PR-B closes).
  - `test_autosave_due_fires_on_max_interval_even_when_idle` — `MAX` and `MAX+1s` with `have_unsaved=false` return true (defensive ceiling preserves legacy behavior).
  - `test_autosave_due_constants_have_expected_values` — pins 30s / 600s budgets and the invariant `QUIET < MAX`.
  Full `cargo test --bin xray --features lang-csharp,lang-typescript,lang-rust` 2197 passed; `cargo clippy --tests -- -D warnings` clean.
- **Reviewer-caught MEDIUM (commit-reviewer subagent, second pass)**: the post-reconcile checkpoint callsite at the top of `start_watcher` still dropped the new `bool` return value via `let _ = periodic_autosave(...)`, so a failed startup save would leave `have_unsaved=false` and the comment's promise that "the next quiet-interval tick will retry" was a lie — the retry could not happen until `AUTOSAVE_MAX_INTERVAL`. **Fix**: capture `saved_ok`, still bump `last_autosave` to throttle, and `if !saved_ok { have_unsaved = true; }` so a failed cold-start save propagates into the loop and the first quiet-interval tick after the watcher starts retries the durability.
- **Reviewer-caught MEDIUM (commit-reviewer subagent, first pass)**: two `start_watcher` exit paths — generation-change and the `Disconnected` channel branch — called `process_batch` and then `break`-ed without saving, so the final batch of dirty files lived only in RAM and was lost on a force-kill timed at the same moment as the watcher tear-down. **Fix**: both exit paths now set `have_unsaved=true` after the best-effort `process_batch` and call `periodic_autosave` once before `break` (best-effort `let _ = ...` because the thread is exiting and there's no retry surface). The 4 in-loop callsites unchanged in placement but now use the conditional-clear pattern below.
- **Reviewer-caught LOW (same first pass)**: `periodic_autosave` returned `()`, so callers cleared `have_unsaved=false` even when the save actually failed (poisoned lock, write error). The next retry would only happen after `AUTOSAVE_MAX_INTERVAL` (10 min), masking the failure for up to 10 minutes — exactly the data-loss window PR-B was supposed to close. **Fix**: `periodic_autosave -> bool` (true = durably consistent / no-op, false = ≥1 save or read failure). Callers always bump `last_autosave = now` (throttle next retry to one `QUIET_INTERVAL` instead of busy-looping) but only `if saved_ok { have_unsaved = false; }` so a transient failure keeps the dirty flag and the next quiet-interval tick retries. New unit tests: `test_periodic_autosave_returns_true_on_success`, `test_periodic_autosave_returns_true_on_empty_indexes`, `test_periodic_autosave_returns_false_on_poisoned_lock` (latter spawns a thread that takes the write lock and panics, then asserts `periodic_autosave` returns false on the poisoned `RwLock`).



### Fix (post-reconcile checkpoint — close the durability window after PR #208)

- **`start_watcher` now persists the new baseline to disk immediately when startup reconciliation actually changed the indexed content or definition state.** PR #208 stopped `xray_info` from *reporting* stale post-removal counters via `live_file_count()`, but the on-disk `.meta` was still only refreshed every `AUTOSAVE_INTERVAL` (10 minutes) by `periodic_autosave` or by graceful shutdown. A forced kill (`Stop-Process -Force`, `cargo install --force` overwriting the binary mid-flight, OS crash, power loss) within that window resurrected the pre-reconcile counter on next start — exactly the ratchet PR #208 fixed at the API layer. **Fix shape (Hole #1 from `user-stories/meta-checkpoint-durability.md`)**: `reconcile_content_index` now returns `(added, modified, removed): (usize, usize, usize)` (mirroring the existing `reconcile_definition_index_nonblocking` signature); `start_watcher` captures both tuples and calls `periodic_autosave` exactly when something actually changed. New helper `post_reconcile_checkpoint_needed(content_added, content_modified, content_removed, def_changed) -> bool` keeps the decision pure and testable. `last_autosave` is bumped after the save so the 10-minute periodic timer doesn't fire a duplicate save shortly after for no reason. Steady-state startups (in-sync workspace) pay zero — the gate evaluates false and no write happens. Out-of-sync startups pay one full `periodic_autosave` (~1.6-3.2s on a 48K-file repo per `docs/benchmarks.md` extrapolation, well under the cost of losing the ratchet fix to a force-kill).
- **Reviewer-caught HIGH (commit-reviewer subagent, 2026-04-25, first pass)**: initial implementation gated on `content_before != content_after` (net live-count delta). That missed the offline-replace case — delete A.cs + add B.cs with no def change keeps `live_file_count` constant but still mutates `idx.files[]` and the inverted index, so a force-kill of session B would let session C load a stale on-disk content index (removed file present, added file missing). **Fix**: gate on add/remove **counts** (`content_added > 0 || content_removed > 0 || def_changed`) instead of net delta. New regression test `test_post_reconcile_checkpoint_needed_triggers_on_content_replace` pins the contract.
- **Reviewer-caught MEDIUM #1 (same first pass)**: e2e `T-CHECKPOINT-AFTER-RECONCILE` originally killed session B as soon as stderr matched `Post-reconcile checkpoint`, but that log is emitted *before* the save call — on a slow box the kill could land mid-save, causing flakes even when product code is correct. **Fix**: wait for `Periodic autosave complete` (emitted after the atomic tmp+rename in `save_compressed`) before killing. Failure-message branches distinguish "never triggered checkpoint" from "triggered but save didn't complete in 8s".
- **Reviewer-caught MEDIUM #2 (commit-reviewer subagent, 2026-04-25, second pass)**: post-HIGH-fix gate `(content_added > 0 || content_removed > 0 || def_changed)` still excluded **modify-only** reconciles. When startup reconciliation finds a file whose content changed offline (mtime > `idx.created_at - 2s`) but the file set is otherwise stable, `reconcile_content_index` rewrites that file's postings in RAM without touching `idx.files[]`. Without a post-reconcile save, force-kill of session B would let session C load the **pre-modify** postings from disk and serve outdated `xray_grep` results until the next periodic autosave (up to 10 minutes). The bug is silent — `xray_info` `files` count is correct, but search results are stale. **Fix**: helper now takes `content_modified` as a fourth argument; gate is `content_added > 0 || content_modified > 0 || content_removed > 0 || def_changed`. New unit test `test_post_reconcile_checkpoint_needed_triggers_on_content_modify` pins the gate; new end-to-end test `test_post_reconcile_checkpoint_writes_postings_after_modify_only` builds an index, saves it, modifies one file's content offline, runs the post-reconcile sequence, reloads the on-disk index, and asserts the new tokens are present in the on-disk inverted index (pre-fix would still serve old tokens).
- **Tests**: `src/mcp/watcher_tests.rs` adds 6 helper unit tests (`test_post_reconcile_checkpoint_needed_triggers_on_content_add`, `..._on_content_removal`, `..._on_content_modify`, `..._on_content_replace`, `..._on_def_change`, `..._skipped_on_noop`) and 2 end-to-end durability tests (`test_post_reconcile_checkpoint_writes_meta_after_removal` — counter durability after offline removal; `test_post_reconcile_checkpoint_writes_postings_after_modify_only` — posting-list durability after offline modify). **End-to-end** regression added in `e2e-test.ps1::T-CHECKPOINT-AFTER-RECONCILE`: build with 3 files → delete 1 file → start `serve --watch` → wait for both `Post-reconcile checkpoint` AND `Periodic autosave complete` log lines → **force-kill** the process → start a fresh `serve` (without `--watch`) → assert `xray_info` content `files=2` purely from the on-disk state the killed session left behind. Pre-fix this scenario would report `files=3`. Full `cargo test --bin xray --features lang-csharp,lang-typescript,lang-rust` 2189 passed; `cargo clippy --tests -- -D warnings` clean.


### Fix (stale `idx.files` counter — cross-session ratchet in `xray_info`)


- **`xray_info`, `IndexMeta`, and audit logs no longer report stale file counts after deletions for either content or definition indexes.** Root cause: `idx.files: Vec<String>` is an append-only file_id allocator (slot 0 = first ever indexed file, slot N = N+1th, never reused — see `src/lib.rs::ContentIndex` and `src/definitions/types.rs::DefinitionIndex`). Removal paths (`reconcile_content_index` Phase 4, `update_content_index` Phase 3, `reconcile_definition_index_nonblocking` Phase 4, `remove_file_from_def_index`) decremented `path_to_id` and `file_token_counts[fid] = 0` but left `idx.files[fid]` untouched. Reporting callsites that used `idx.files.len()` (`handle_xray_info`, `content_index_meta`, `definition_index_meta`, `estimate_*_memory`, `summary["indexFiles"]`, `serve` startup logs, `periodic_autosave`, shutdown log) thus reported allocator capacity, not live count. The drift was persisted across sessions via `IndexMeta.files` in the `.meta` files, ratcheting upward every reconcile cycle (observed `files=770` for ~166 live files). See `user-stories/stale-content-index-files-counter.md`.
- **Fix shape**: keep `idx.files` strictly append-only (file_id stability is depended on by `idx.files[fid]` lookups in callers/grep formatting and by serialized indexes), but now **tombstone the slot via `String::clear()`** at every removal site so `idx.files[fid]` of a removed file becomes `""`. Add `live_file_count()` as the **single source of truth** for user-visible counts: `ContentIndex` returns `path_to_id.len()` when present, falling back to `files.iter().filter(|s| !s.is_empty()).count()` for cold-loaded indexes; `DefinitionIndex` returns `path_to_id.len()`. Replace every reporting callsite. `build_watch_index_from` filters empty paths defensively so a legacy on-disk index loaded into the new code doesn't resurrect tombstones into `path_to_id`. **`CONTENT_INDEX_VERSION` / `DEFINITION_INDEX_VERSION` NOT bumped** — `IndexMeta.files` is informational, not consulted during index reconstruction; first save after fix overwrites the stale meta with the correct count.
- **Reviewer-caught regressions, fixed in same change** (commit-reviewer subagent, 2026-04-24): (a) `periodic_autosave` originally gated on `live_file_count() > 0` — that **skipped** checkpointing an index whose final file had just been removed, allowing the previous on-disk snapshot to resurrect on forced kill. Reverted gate to `!idx.files.is_empty()` (allocator-capacity semantic = "has this index ever held a file"). New regression test `test_periodic_autosave_checkpoints_post_removal_empty_index` pins the contract. (b) `estimate_content_index_memory` / `estimate_definition_index_memory` originally multiplied `live_files` by per-file bytes — but `String::clear()` keeps the heap capacity, so tombstoned slots still consume the original bytes. Switched `files_mb` math to `idx.files.len()` (allocator capacity, reflects actual heap residency); `fileCount` in the JSON output stays as `live_files` (user-visible count).
- **Tests**: `src/mcp/watcher_tests.rs` adds `live_file_count_matches_path_to_id_after_removal`, `live_file_count_falls_back_to_files_when_no_path_to_id`, `build_watch_index_skips_tombstoned_slots`, `content_index_meta_uses_live_count_after_removal`, `test_periodic_autosave_checkpoints_post_removal_empty_index`. `src/definitions/definitions_tests.rs` adds `def_live_file_count_matches_path_to_id_after_removal`, `def_live_file_count_falls_back_to_path_to_id`, `def_index_meta_uses_live_count_after_removal` (lang-csharp gated where applicable). `src/index_tests.rs` adds `estimate_content_index_memory_uses_live_count_with_tombstones`, `estimate_definition_index_memory_uses_live_count_with_tombstones`. **End-to-end** regression added in `e2e-test.ps1::T-INFO-NO-STALE-FILES-AFTER-REMOVAL`: two-session scenario (build with 3 files → save+exit → delete 1 file between sessions → restart with `--watch` → assert `xray_info` content `files=2` AND stderr proves the index was loaded from disk, not silently rebuilt from FS — the rebuild-fallback would have masked the bug). Two pre-existing tests had fixtures that relied on the buggy `files.len()` semantic (empty `path_to_id` + populated `files`) — fixed by populating `path_to_id` to match. Full `cargo test --bin xray --features lang-csharp,lang-typescript,lang-rust` 2181 passed; `cargo clippy --tests -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo check --workspace --no-default-features --locked` clean.


### Documentation/Bench (PERF-AUDIT-2026-04-24 follow-ups: FIX-7/8/9 — representativeness + clarity)

- **`bench_resolve_parent_substring` (benches/search_benchmarks.rs) renamed to `callers_resolve_substring_memo_shape` and clearly scoped.** PERF-AUDIT FIX-7: the bench's inner substring scan is `for k in idx2.index.keys() { if k.contains(cls) }` — a linear key walk, not the trigram-intersection path production's `collect_substring_file_ids` (`src/mcp/handlers/callers.rs` ~lines 1483/1495/1508) actually uses. As written, the bench correctly demonstrates the *memoisation* speed-up (the PERF-07 win) but does NOT measure real lookup latency. Renamed the criterion group and added a multi-paragraph doc comment that (a) calls out what the bench is measuring (memoisation shape) and (b) explicitly warns the numbers are an upper bound, with a TODO to add a separate naive-vs-trigram bench in a follow-up. **No code change** — measurement scope hygiene only.
- **`docs/architecture.md` trigram pipeline diagram clarified.** PERF-AUDIT FIX-8 / DOC-01: the mermaid edge label `sort + dedup posting lists` was ambiguous — read literally it suggested file-level work deduplication. Renamed to `sort + dedup token-idx lists` and added a paragraph explaining that the dedup removes duplicate token indices arising from sliding-window overlap within a single token (e.g. `"abcabc"` produces trigram `"abc"` twice via the sliding window). The dedup is correctness-of-posting-list (no duplicate token-idx entries), not file-level work-saving — each surviving token-idx still resolves to its full posting list downstream.
- **`scripts/bench-git-perf.ps1` PERF-04 + PERF-09 bench shapes corrected.** PERF-AUDIT FIX-9: (1) PERF-04 used `--format=%H` which measures hash-listing cost — production `top_authors` parses `%an|%ae` lines, so the prior bench under-reported real cold cost. Switched to `--format='%an|%ae'` and renamed the row. (2) PERF-09 measures `git blame --porcelain` subprocess cost only — the actual `parse_blame_porcelain` parser is in Rust and cannot be exercised from a PS harness. Renamed the row to `PERF-09 git blame --porcelain subprocess only (parser excluded)` with a comment explaining the bench is an upper bound on what xray could ever achieve for that file (parser cost is added on top, not subtracted). Smoke-tested both with `-Iterations 3` against a fresh tempdir repo.


### Fix (PERF-00 follow-up: bench-git-perf median + Iterations guard)


- **`scripts/bench-git-perf.ps1` `Measure-Cmd` now reports the classical median and rejects non-positive `Iterations`.** Two PERF-AUDIT-2026-04-24 review findings: (1) `$sorted[[int]($sorted.Count / 2)]` always picked the upper-middle element — for an even-N sample (e.g. 4 iterations) it returned `sorted[2]` (the 3rd value) instead of `(sorted[1] + sorted[2]) / 2`.
