This biased reported medians upward and made `-Iterations 4` (the obvious sweet-spot for fast smoke runs) silently produce a different statistic than `-Iterations 5`. (2) `-Iterations 0` was accepted, the for-loop ran zero times, `$sorted` was empty, and the median index lookup returned `$null` formatted as `0` — a meaningless measurement that could be mistaken for sub-millisecond performance. **Fix**: classical median (average of two middles for even N, single middle for odd N) + a `[ValidateRange(1, [int]::MaxValue)]` attribute on the `-Iterations` script parameter (rejects 0 / negative at param binding) + a defensive `if ($Iterations -lt 1) { throw }` inside `Measure-Cmd` for callers that import the function. Smoke-tested with `-Iterations 4` (real measurement) and `-Iterations 0` (rejected before any work). No production code change — measurement script only.


### Fix (PERF-02 follow-up: drop negative cache to enable self-healing)


- **`detect_main_branch_name` no longer caches `None` results.** PERF-02 originally cached `Some(None)` for paths where the probe found neither `main` nor `master`, intending to skip re-spawning git on a known-hopeless path. **Bug**: this permanently poisoned any path probed before its repo existed. A handler that runs `detect_main_branch_name` against an empty workspace, then the user `git init`-s the directory and creates a `main` branch, would forever return None until server restart — a real recovery scenario, not a corner case (LSP attach to an empty folder, then user opens a terminal and inits the repo). **Fix**: only insert into `branch_name_cache` when `resolved.is_some()`. Cost: a repeated probe of a still-bad path now spawns one `git for-each-ref` per request (≈5-20 ms on Windows) — paid only by the rare bad-path case; the common positive path remains zero-spawn on warm calls. Updated `branch_name_cache` field doc to spell out the new contract. **Tests in `src/mcp/handlers/git_handler_tests.rs`**: renamed `test_detect_main_branch_name_caches_negative_result` → `test_detect_main_branch_name_does_not_cache_negative_result` (asserts the bad path is **absent** from the cache map); new `test_detect_main_branch_name_self_heals_after_git_init` (tempdir, probes pre-init → None + no cache entry, runs `git init -b main` + commit, probes again → `Some("main")` — pre-fix this would have stayed None forever); rewrote `test_detect_main_branch_name_keys_by_repo_path` to use two real tempdir repos (the old test relied on negative caching of a fake path to get to count=2). Full bin suite 2170 tests + clippy `--all-targets -D warnings` clean.


### Fix (PERF-04 follow-up: deterministic tie-break + coverage gaps closed)


- **`top_authors` ranking is now fully deterministic on tied commit counts.** PERF-04 (commit `490b036`) changed the aggregation HashMap key from `format!("{} <{}>", name, email)` String to `(String, String)` tuple. The sort was `sort_by_key(|b| Reverse(b.count))` — stable but with no secondary key, so authors with equal commit counts came out in HashMap iteration order. Iteration order depends on the hash of the key type, so the key swap silently flipped tie ordering between callers (snapshot tests / paginated UIs / golden output). **Fix**: replace the single-key sort with a fully-specified comparator: `Reverse(count) → name asc → email asc`. Also closes the FIX-10 test-coverage gap from the same review: 3 new tempdir-based regression tests cover (a) tie-break ordering with two authors at 1 commit each (Alice before Bob), (b) same-name-different-email counted as 2 distinct authors with email-asc tie-break, (c) different-name-same-email counted as 2 distinct authors. Required new test helper `commit_as` because the existing `run_git` hardcodes `GIT_AUTHOR_*` env vars to a single test identity (incompatible with multi-author scenarios). Existing 3 PERF-04 tests pass unchanged. Full bin suite 2169 tests + clippy `--all-targets -D warnings` clean.


### Fix (PERF-03 follow-up: --first-parent for merge commits in get_commit_diff)


- **`get_commit_diff` now passes `--first-parent` to `git show` so merge commits emit a non-empty patch.** PERF-03 (commit `bcaf44f`) collapsed the parent-probe + diff sequence into a single `git show <hash> --format= --patch -- <file>`. For non-merge commits this is byte-identical to the legacy `git diff <hash>^..<hash>`, but for **merge commits** `git show` defaults to a *combined diff* that prunes paths uninteresting against AT LEAST ONE parent. A typical feature→main merge that takes the feature side produces an EMPTY patch under combined-diff (the merge result equals one parent's tree on every touched file), while `git diff <hash>^..<hash>` always followed first-parent and emitted the trunk-vs-merge diff. Net effect on `xray_git_history file=… includeDiff=true`: merge commits returned in the no-follow fallback path (deleted files, or any callsite that disables follow) silently dropped their patch text. Verified empirically with a temp repo (`merge --strategy-option=theirs` + manual resolution): default `git show` returned 0 lines, `git show --first-parent` matched `git diff HEAD^..HEAD` exactly. **Fix**: add `--first-parent` to the `git show` invocation. For non-merge commits the flag is a no-op (only one parent exists); for merges it restores the legacy single-parent diff. **Test**: new regression `test_get_commit_diff_merge_commit_uses_first_parent` builds a real tempdir repo with a manually-resolved merge (resolution distinct from both parents to bypass `git log` history simplification), grabs the merge SHA via `git rev-parse HEAD`, and calls `get_commit_diff` directly — asserting the patch contains both `-v2-main` and `+v2-merged`. Pre-fix this assertion would have triggered with an empty patch. Existing 3 PERF-03 tests pass unchanged. Full bin suite 2166 tests + clippy `--all-targets -D warnings` clean.


### Fix (PERF-08 follow-up: preserve mid-build watcher invalidation)


- **`ensure_file_index` no longer loses watcher signals that arrive while a build is in flight.** PERF-08 (commit `b551f2f`) cleared `file_index_dirty` *after* publishing the new index via an unconditional `store(false)` at the end of the build path. If a watcher set `dirty=true` *during* the in-flight build, the builder's tail `store(false)` overwrote that signal in the same AtomicBool slot — the next `xray_fast` caller observed `dirty=false, file_index=Some` and **skipped the rebuild**, serving the now-stale snapshot until the next watcher event after the build finished. **Fix**: swap `dirty=false` *before* running `build_fn` (not after). Mid-build watcher signals re-arm `dirty=true` and the next caller correctly rebuilds. Two RAII guards keep the invariant tight: `BuildSlotGuard` (already there) clears `building=false` on every exit, and the new `DirtyRestoreGuard` puts `dirty=true` back if the build does NOT complete successfully (early `?` return, panic), so a transient build error doesn't permanently lose the invalidation it would otherwise have re-triggered. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/utils_tests.rs::ensure_file_index_tests`: `test_ensure_file_index_preserves_mid_build_dirty_signal` (build closure sets `dirty=true` mid-build → asserts dirty observable as true after first call AND second call rebuilds, total `build_count == 2`); `test_ensure_file_index_restores_dirty_on_build_error` (build returns `Err` → asserts `dirty` restored to its pre-build value via `DirtyRestoreGuard`, index still `None`). Existing 4 PERF-08 tests pass unchanged. Full bin suite 2165 tests + clippy `--all-targets -D warnings` clean.


### Fix (PERF-02 follow-up: explicit priority order for main-branch detection)


- **`probe_main_branch_name` no longer trusts `git for-each-ref` to emit refs in argument order.** PERF-02 (commit `b751f78`) collapsed the cold probe into one `git for-each-ref refs/heads/main refs/heads/master refs/remotes/origin/main refs/remotes/origin/master` call and `return`-ed on the **first** matching line, on the (false) assumption that git emits hits in the order the refs were listed. `for-each-ref` actually sorts its output by refname, so a repo with `refs/heads/master` + `refs/remotes/origin/main` (and no local `main`) emitted `master` *before* `origin/main` and `detect_main_branch_name` returned `"master"` — flipping `behindMain` / `aheadOfMain` in `handle_branch_status` onto the wrong upstream for that (common) layout. Legacy 4-probe semantics always preferred `main` (local-or-remote) over `master` (local-or-remote). **Fix**: enumerate which of the four candidates `for-each-ref` returned, then apply explicit priority `main → master`, restoring legacy semantics in one spawn instead of four. Misleading docstring (claimed arg-ordered output) corrected at the same time. **Test**: new regression `test_detect_main_branch_name_prefers_main_over_local_master` builds a real tempdir repo via `git init -b master` + `git update-ref refs/remotes/origin/main HEAD`, then asserts `detect_main_branch_name` returns `Some("main")` — pre-fix this test would have asserted `Some("master")` (verified by reproducing the git output manually before writing the fix). Existing 4 PERF-02 cache tests still pass; full bin suite 2163 tests + lib 105 tests + clippy `--all-targets -D warnings` clean.


### Performance (PERF-08: single-flight guard for xray_fast file-index rebuild)

- **`xray_fast` lazy file-index rebuild now serialises through a single-flight gate (`Mutex<bool> + Condvar`).** Pre-PERF-08 the handler did `if needs_rebuild { build_index(...); store(...); }` with no mutual exclusion. Under N concurrent `xray_fast` calls on a cold or watcher-invalidated context, every thread observed `needs_rebuild=true` (because the others hadn't finished writing yet) and **each one ran a full filesystem walk + ~8 MB allocation + on-disk save in parallel**. On a 100k-file repo with 4-8 concurrent LLM tool calls this multiplied cold-start cost by ~N (~5-15 s stall instead of one 2-5 s build), plus N redundant disk writes that each clobbered the previous result. **Fix**: extracted the rebuild into `mcp::handlers::utils::ensure_file_index(ctx, build_fn)` which takes a tiny mutex around state inspection only — exactly one thread owns the build slot and runs `build_fn` lock-free, while other waiters block on a `Condvar` and wake to re-check (returning immediately if the in-flight build succeeded, or taking over the slot if it failed). The expensive `build_index` call runs **outside** the mutex, so unrelated `xray_fast` requests against an already-built non-dirty index never touch the gate at all. **Reset semantics** (the explicit reason `tokio::sync::OnceCell` was rejected): the gate is a transient guard, not the index owner — after each build the `building` flag returns to `false` and the next watcher signal (`file_index_dirty=true`) re-triggers exactly one rebuild with the same single-flight guarantee. **Panic safety**: the build slot is held via a `BuildSlotGuard` RAII type whose `Drop` clears `building=false` and `notify_all`s waiters even on unwind, so a panic inside `build_index` cannot strand waiters forever — they wake, see `file_index` still `None`, and one of them takes over. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/utils_tests.rs::ensure_file_index_tests`: (1) `test_ensure_file_index_single_flight_cold_start_16_threads` — 16 threads barrier-synced into a brand-new `HandlerContext` with a 50 ms build closure; asserts `build_count == 1`, `file_index.is_some()`, `dirty == false`. (2) `test_ensure_file_index_single_flight_after_dirty_signal` — cold race + watcher invalidation + second 16-thread race; asserts total build count == 2 (1 cold + 1 rebuild), proving reset semantics. (3) `test_ensure_file_index_recovers_after_builder_panic` — first call panics inside the build closure, caught via `catch_unwind`; asserts gate is released (`building == false`), index is still `None`, and a second call succeeds (proving the RAII guard prevented permanent deadlock). (4) `test_ensure_file_index_skips_build_when_fresh` — with a pre-populated non-dirty index, the build closure must NOT run (defensive fast-path guard). All 4 pass; full suite 2162 binary tests + 105 lib tests + 1 doctest zero regressions; clippy `--all-targets -D warnings` clean. Wiring: new field `HandlerContext.file_index_build_gate: Arc<utils::FileIndexBuildGate>` plumbed through all 3 construction sites (`Default` impl in `src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs`, production init in `src/cli/serve.rs`, test init in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests.rs`).


### Performance (PERF-05: ASCII fast-path for generate_trigrams)

- **`generate_trigrams` skips the intermediate `Vec<char>` allocation for ASCII tokens.** The vast majority of tokens fed into the trigram index are ASCII identifiers (code symbols, log lines, English text). Pre-PERF-05 every call paid for `chars().collect::<Vec<char>>()` (a heap `Vec` of 4-byte `char` per code unit, e.g. 56 bytes for a 14-char identifier like `HandlerContext`) plus a per-window `iter().collect::<String>()` (heap `String` per trigram). The `Vec<char>` step is pure overhead for ASCII because each byte == one char by definition. **Fix**: front-load `if token.is_ascii() { … }` and slide directly over `token.as_bytes().windows(3)`, with `std::str::from_utf8(w).unwrap().to_string()` per trigram (the validation walk on 3 bytes is negligible vs. the heap allocation that follows it; staying with safe code rather than `from_utf8_unchecked` to avoid an `unsafe` block for marginal gain). Non-ASCII tokens (Cyrillic, CJK, emoji) keep the original char-based path verbatim — code-unit windows would split multi-byte UTF-8 sequences mid-codepoint, so the slow path is mandatory there. **Tests**: `test_generate_trigrams_ascii_fast_path_parity` (in `src/lib_tests.rs`) builds the expected trigram list manually for an ASCII identifier and asserts byte-for-byte equality with `generate_trigrams("HandlerContext")` — including order, which the index relies on. The same test then runs `generate_trigrams("abПривет")` (mixed ASCII + Cyrillic, must take the slow path) and asserts (a) result length matches the char-count formula `chars-2`, (b) first two trigrams are `"abП"` and `"bПр"` (proves char-aligned, not byte-aligned), (c) every trigram is exactly 3 codepoints (would fail if the fast-path mistakenly fired on multi-byte input). Existing 12 trigram tests + Greek `αβγδ` test + 2158 binary tests + 105 lib tests all pass unchanged. Clippy clean. The `bench_generate_trigrams` group from PERF-00 (`benches/search_benchmarks.rs`) is the perf measurement instrument — run before/after to quantify the speedup on `ascii_short_17`, `ascii_medium_45`, `ascii_long_120`, `vocab_18k_tokens` (ASCII paths) and confirm `cyrillic_18chars` / `cjk_7chars` (Unicode paths) are unchanged.


### Performance (PERF-04: top_authors tuple key)

- **`top_authors` author-aggregation map keyed on `(String, String)` instead of a `format!`-built display string.** Pre-PERF-04 each commit in the input stream paid a `format!("{} <{}>", commit.author_name, commit.author_email)` String allocation just to build a HashMap key — but the formatted display string was never used after the lookup (it was only consumed by `entry(key)`, then `InternalStats.name` / `.email` carried the unformatted parts forward). On a 50k-commit / 50-author repo (the realistic upper bound under the 50000 `--max-count` cap) that's ~49,950 redundant String allocations + format calls per `top_authors` invocation, all wasted work. **Fix**: switch the HashMap key to the tuple `(commit.author_name.clone(), commit.author_email.clone())` — same uniqueness semantics (both fields disambiguate authors) but no format step, and the display string never needs to exist. `InternalStats` already stored `name` and `email` as separate fields so no information is lost. **Tests**: zero new assertions needed — the existing `top_authors` test triplet (`test_top_authors_returns_ranked`, `test_top_authors_with_filter`, `test_top_authors_with_path`) already asserts post-aggregation correctness (count, ranking, fields), and they all pass unchanged. Clippy clean.


### Performance (PERF-03: get_commit_diff via git show)

- **`get_commit_diff` collapses parent-probe + diff into a single `git show` spawn (and stops hard-coding the magic empty-tree SHA).** Pre-PERF-03 each per-commit patch fetch on `xray_git_history file=… includeDiff=true` cost two git spawns: (1) `git rev-parse --verify <hash>^` to detect whether the commit had a parent, then (2) either `git diff <hash>^..<hash>` (normal) or `git diff 4b825dc6…<empty-tree>… <hash>` (initial commit). On 200-commit history fetches that's 400 spawns ≈ 1–4 s wasted on Windows process-creation. Worse, the empty-tree SHA `4b825dc642cb6eb9a060e54bf899d69f7cb0cb10` is **not always present** in a clone — it only resolves when the empty tree object is reachable from a ref, so freshly-init'd repos with a single initial commit could fail with `bad object 4b825dc6…` even on perfectly valid input (verified by reproducing on the xray repo before the fix). **Fix**: replace the whole branch with `git show <hash> --format= --patch -- <file>`, which (a) handles the no-parent case natively (diff against `/dev/null`, no parent required, no magic SHA), (b) collapses parent-probe + diff into one spawn, (c) produces patch-section output that is **byte-identical** to `git diff <hash>^..<hash>` for non-initial commits — verified pre-merge by walking real history on the xray repo (length + content matched on 3 sample commits, see `bench-git-perf.ps1` for the harness). Truncation at `MAX_PATCH_LINES` is preserved verbatim. **Tests** in `src/git/git_tests.rs`: `test_file_history_with_diff_includes_initial_commit_patch` builds a tempdir repo with exactly one commit and asserts the returned patch contains `new file mode` + `--- /dev/null` (proves git show handled the no-parent case without the empty-tree SHA — pre-PERF-03 code path could fail here in some repo states); `test_file_history_with_diff_normal_commit_patch_shape` builds a 2-commit tempdir repo and asserts the v2 commit's patch contains `-v1` + `+v2` and does NOT contain `new file mode` (regression guard against any future refactor that accidentally emits new-file headers for normal modifications). Existing `test_file_history_with_diff` still passes. Full git module suite (221 tests) zero regressions, clippy clean.


### Performance (PERF-02: cached + collapsed main-branch detection)

- **`xray_branch_status` no longer pays 4 sequential `git rev-parse` per request — combined into one `git for-each-ref` and the result is cached per repo path.** `detect_main_branch_name` previously spawned up to 4 sequential `git rev-parse --verify` invocations (`main`, `refs/remotes/origin/main`, `master`, `refs/remotes/origin/master`) on every `xray_branch_status` call — ~5–20 ms per spawn on Windows process-creation = ~20–80 ms wasted per request, and the answer is invariant for the lifetime of the repo. **Fix**: (a) collapse the cold probe into a single `git for-each-ref --format=%(refname:short) refs/heads/main refs/heads/master refs/remotes/origin/main refs/remotes/origin/master` call (one spawn instead of up to four; legacy 4-probe sequence kept as a fallback if `for-each-ref` ever fails for any reason — very old git, hardened sandbox — so resolution behaviour is byte-identical to pre-PERF-02); (b) cache the result on `HandlerContext.branch_name_cache: Arc<RwLock<HashMap<String, Option<String>>>>` keyed by the raw repo string the caller passed (no canonicalisation — that would itself be a syscall on Windows). Negative results (`Some(None)`) are cached too so a known-hopeless path doesn't keep re-spawning git on every request. **Invalidation contract**: keyed by repo path, so workspace switches naturally miss-then-repopulate. Known limitation documented on the cache field: a long-running session that does `git branch -d main` after the cache populated will still report `mainBranch=\"main\"` until the server restarts — acceptable trade-off because the destructive rename is a manual one-shot action and the previous behaviour was 4× spawn cost indefinitely. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/git_handler_tests.rs`: `test_detect_main_branch_name_populates_cache_on_first_call` (pins single-entry cache state after first call), `test_detect_main_branch_name_returns_cached_value_without_reprobe` (fakes a `\"trunk\"` cache entry and asserts the function returns it instead of probing — guards against a future refactor silently bypassing the cache lookup), `test_detect_main_branch_name_caches_negative_result` (asserts bad-repo `None` is stored as `Some(None)` so warm-path lookups short-circuit), `test_detect_main_branch_name_keys_by_repo_path` (per-repo isolation pin = workspace-switch invalidation contract). Existing 6 `branch_status` integration tests + full 2156-test unit suite zero regressions.


### Documentation (DOC-01: trigram rebuild locking discipline)

- **`docs/architecture.md` — trigram lazy-rebuild section now matches the actual `ensure_trigram_index` implementation.** Pre-edit the doc claimed "rebuilt from scratch (~200ms)" with no mention of the locking strategy, which made it look like the rebuild blocks all readers under a write-lock for the duration. The current code (`src/mcp/handlers/grep.rs::ensure_trigram_index`, landed earlier this year) builds the new `TrigramIndex` under the **read** lock (concurrent `xray_grep` / `xray_callers` queries continue without contention), then takes the write-lock only to swap the pointer and flip the dirty flag (microseconds), with a double-checked `trigram_dirty` re-test inside the write critical section to drop duplicate work if two readers raced into rebuild. Updated the "Watcher Integration (Lazy Rebuild)" subsection to spell this out, added a small ASCII diagram of the read-lock / write-lock / read-lock sequence, and updated the "Lazy / On-Demand Rebuild" table row so it no longer carries the misleading "~200ms" absolute. The rebuild itself is still the dominant cost of the request that triggers it; what changed (and what the doc now reflects) is that other readers are no longer stalled by it. No code change.


### Performance (PERF-AUDIT-2026-04-24 baseline harness)

- **PERF-00 — extend benchmarks for the perf-audit story (no production code change).** Added four micro-bench groups in `benches/search_benchmarks.rs` covering the hot paths targeted by the [PERF-AUDIT-2026-04-24 story](docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_perf-audit-followups.md): `generate_trigrams` (PERF-05, ASCII fast-path candidate + Cyrillic/CJK regression guards + 18k-vocab build), `regex_compile` (PERF-01, per-request `Regex::new` cost across the TV/PH/LR sites vs cached match-only reference), `top_authors_aggregation` (PERF-04, `format!` per-commit key vs tuple key over 50k synthetic commits), and `callers_resolve_substring` (PERF-07, naïve per-node lookup + substring scan vs memoised resolution over 100 simulated tree nodes). Spawn-bound git paths (PERF-02 `detect_main_branch_name`, PERF-03 `get_commit_diff`, PERF-09 `parse_blame_porcelain`, PERF-04 raw `git log` cost) are deliberately measured outside criterion via the new `scripts/bench-git-perf.ps1` harness — criterion + `git` subprocess produces high-variance numbers and bakes in repo-state coupling we don't want in the harness. `docs/benchmarks.md` gains a "PERF-AUDIT-2026-04-24 baselines" section documenting how to capture and diff against the `pre-perf-audit` baseline plus a bench-to-task mapping. End-to-end MCP handler latency is intentionally out of scope (would require a `bench-internals` feature flag exposing `HandlerContext` — deferred to a follow-up so this PR stays additive and zero-API-surface).


### Bug Fixes (advisory + edit correctness ripple-grep 2026-04-24)

Cross-review follow-ups to the `three-correctness-followups` and `hardening` bundles below — each item is a sibling/nested case the original fix did not enumerate, caught by re-walking the contract surfaces (predicates, hint strings, line-count semantics, error-priority order). All four ship in one commit because they touch the same two files (`advisory_hints.rs`, `edit.rs`) and share the same root cause: narrow-spec trap (the original story described one shape of the bug; the same predicate can be reached through one more path).

- **`xray_callers` `interface_vias_caveat` — no longer merges interface facts across unrelated same-short-name concrete types** (closes Problem 1 of `user-stories/xray-advisory-hints-namespace-collision-and-yml-gap.md`). Pre-fix, `interface_vias_caveat(class=Foo, …)` resolved `class` through `name_index.get("foo")` and aggregated `base_types` across **every** matching `Class | Struct | Record` entry — so a codebase with `A.Foo : IFoo` and `B.Foo : IBar` got a hint claiming the targeted `Foo` "implements interface(s): `IFoo`, `IBar`" and recommending `class=IFoo` (which may belong to the OTHER `Foo`). That presented merged facts as if they apply to the selected class. **Fix**: collect the matching concrete defs first; the single-match path keeps the original wording verbatim; the N>1 path switches to ambiguity-aware wording that (a) explicitly announces "{N} types named `Foo` exist", (b) lists each candidate as `Parent.Name (file)` so the caller can disambiguate by inspection, (c) reports the *union* of interfaces with an explicit "some may not apply to the type you targeted" caveat, (d) drops the concrete `class={Iface}` recipe (the suggested interface might belong to a different `Foo` than the user targeted). N>1 with no interfaces returns `None` (nothing useful to suggest). **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/advisory_hints.rs`: `interface_vias_emits_ambiguity_notice_for_duplicate_short_name` (two `Foo` in different namespaces → hint contains "2 types named `Foo`", lists both `Ns.A.Foo (a/Foo.cs)` / `Ns.B.Foo (b/Foo.cs)`, surfaces `IFoo` + `IBar` as union, contains "some may not apply", does NOT contain `class=IFoo` / `class=IBar`), `interface_vias_returns_none_when_ambiguous_and_no_interfaces` (N>1 + zero interfaces → no hint). New test helper `build_index_with_parents` (with `DefSpec` type alias to satisfy `clippy::type_complexity`) populates `parent` and per-def `file_id` so the `Parent.Name (file)` candidate strings can be asserted.

- **`value_source_hint` — suggested grep extension list now includes `yml`** (closes Problem 2 of the same story). The hint emits `xray_grep terms='…' ext='xml,json,config,yaml,manifestxml'` as a ready-to-paste command. Helm charts, GitLab CI, GitHub Actions workflows, k8s manifests, Azure Pipelines, and Ansible playbooks all use `.yml` (NOT `.yaml`) routinely — so the omission caused silent false negatives in exactly the scenario the hint exists to help with. **Fix**: one-line change to `ext='xml,json,config,yaml,yml,manifestxml'`. The existing `value_source_hint_fires_for_property_with_attribute_literal` test was updated to pin the new ext list (`ext='xml,json,config,yaml,yml,manifestxml'`) with a comment noting why `yml` is mandatory.

- **`xray_edit` Mode A — blank-line-only files no longer have a phantom addressable second line; line-count semantics now agree with `count_lines()` across all files** (closes `user-stories/xray-edit-blank-line-only-file-line-count-drift.md`). The 2026-04-23 hardening bundle added a carve-out for the empty-file case (`if lines == [""] { 0 } else { lines.len() }`) but left the adjacent blank-line-only case (`"\n"` → `["", ""]`, len 2) reporting `originalLineCount: 1` while Mode A range validation saw 2 addressable lines — REPLACE 1..2 / DELETE 2 silently succeeded against a phantom slot. The same off-by-one applied to every file ending in `\n` (e.g. `"a\n"` → `["a", ""]`, len 2 → Mode A allowed REPLACE on phantom line 2, while `count_lines` and the response said "1 line"). The earlier carve-out closed only the `""` corner; this generalization closes the whole class. **Fix**: replace `let line_count = if lines == [""] { 0 } else { lines.len() }` with `let line_count = if lines.last() == Some(&"") { lines.len().saturating_sub(1) } else { lines.len() }` — same rule as `count_lines()` (drop trailing-empty sentinel from `split('\n')`). INSERT mode (`startLine: 1, endLine: 0`) is unaffected and remains the canonical write-into-empty path. **Test update**: `test_mode_a_insert_at_end_of_file` previously documented the OLD off-by-one explicitly (passed `startLine: 4, endLine: 3` against `"line1\nline2\n"` because `split('\n')` had 3 elements); rewritten to use the human-aligned coordinates (`startLine: 3, endLine: 2`) with a comment explaining why the phantom slot is gone. **New tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/edit_tests.rs`: `test_blank_line_only_file_lf_treated_as_one_line` (`"\n"`: REPLACE 1..2 errors with "out of range"), `test_blank_line_only_file_crlf_treated_as_one_line` (`"\r\n"`: same), `test_blank_line_only_file_round_trip_line_counts_agree` (`expectedLineCount: 1` + REPLACE 1..1 succeeds — addresses the only legitimate addressable line).

- **`xray_edit` — out-of-range `occurrence` now reports the canonical "found only N time(s)" diagnostic BEFORE `expectedContext` validation runs** (closes `user-stories/xray-edit-expected-context-masks-occurrence-out-of-range.md`). Pre-fix `apply_literal_replace` clamped `target_idx` to 0 for out-of-range `occurrence` "so the context check doesn't panic before the canonical error fires below" (per the inline comment) — but then immediately ran `check_expected_context(positions[0], …)`. If the supplied context disagreed with the *first* match's surroundings, the user got `Expected context …` for a match they never targeted, masking the more fundamental "you targeted occurrence 99 but only 2 matches exist" error. Code contradicted its own comment. **Fix**: hoist the `if edit.occurrence > count → Err("Occurrence N requested …")` check out of the per-mode (flex_re vs. literal) match arms and place it BEFORE the `expectedContext` block. Both the flex-regex and the literal branches now share the same single guard, and the inline `target_idx` calc inside the context block becomes infallible (`if occurrence == 0 { 0 } else { occurrence - 1 }` — out-of-range cannot reach here). **Test** in `src/mcp/handlers/edit_tests.rs::test_occurrence_out_of_range_reported_before_expected_context_mismatch` (file with 2 `Foo` matches, `occurrence: 99 + expectedContext: "context that does not exist anywhere"` → asserts the response contains `Occurrence 99 requested` AND `found only 2 time(s)` AND does NOT contain `Expected context`, file unchanged on disk).


### Bug Fixes (three-correctness-followups bundle 2026-04-24)

- **`xray_git_activity` includeDeleted CLI — `summary.totalEntries` matches the filtered `activity[].commitCount` sum, not the unfiltered baseline** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_git-activity-includeDeleted-cli-summary-count-mismatch.md`). Pre-fix, `handle_git_activity` derived `total_entries` from the in-memory `file_map: HashMap<PathBuf, Vec<...>>` BEFORE the deleted-files filter ran, but `files_array` (what the response actually returns) was filtered down to deleted paths only when `includeDeleted=true`. Result: a CLI-path call with `includeDeleted=true` over a repo with 5 commits across 5 files (3 deleted) returned `activity[].length == 3`, the per-file `commitCount` summed to 3, but `summary.totalEntries == 5` — visibly inconsistent and indistinguishable from a true "5 commits" answer downstream. Cache-path callers were unaffected because `pruned_total_commits` is recomputed from the post-filter set after pruning. **Fix**: compute `total_entries` from `files_array.iter().map(|f| f["commitCount"].as_u64().unwrap_or(0) as usize).sum()` so CLI and cache paths agree. **Test** in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests_git.rs::test_git_activity_cli_include_deleted_total_entries_matches_filtered_activity` builds a real tempdir repo with 1 surviving file (2 commits, in HEAD) + 1 deleted file (3 commits), forces the CLI path via `noCache=true` + `make_empty_ctx()`, baselines the unfiltered activity at 2 files / 5 entries, then asserts the `includeDeleted=true` response has exactly 1 file in `activity` AND `summary.totalEntries == 3` (the filtered legacy commit count, not 5).

- **`xray_grep dir=<file>` auto-convert — uses exact-basename match, not substring (no more sibling leak)** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_grep-dir-file-autoconvert-substring-sibling-leak.md`). Pre-fix, when a caller passed `dir=path/to/Service.cs` (a single file), `parse_grep_args` auto-converted to `dir=path/to + file=Service.cs` via `dirAutoConverted`, but `passes_file_filters` interpreted `file=Service.cs` as a substring against the full path AND basename — so any sibling matching the substring (`MyService.cs`, `OldService.cs`, …) was returned alongside the user's intended single file. Callers shaping a query as "search inside this one file" got a wider scope than they specified, with no warning. The substring semantics are intentional for explicit `file=` queries (comma-OR + partial matches); the auto-converted case is the only path where the caller's intent is unambiguously "this exact file". **Fix**: `GrepSearchParams` and `ParsedGrepArgs` gain a `file_filter_exact: bool`. `parse_grep_args` sets it to `true` ONLY in the auto-convert branch (`file_filter.is_none() && !filename.is_empty()` after splitting `dir`). `passes_file_filters` branches on the flag: exact mode requires `basename_lower == file_sub.to_lowercase()`; substring mode preserves the original comma-OR behavior against full path + basename. The `dirAutoConverted` advisory note is still emitted so callers see the rewrite happened. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests_grep.rs`: `test_grep_dir_as_file_auto_convert_uses_exact_basename_not_substring_siblings` (3 .cs files all containing the marker, `dir=tmp/Service.cs` returns exactly 1 match, `dirAutoConverted` note still present), `test_grep_explicit_file_filter_keeps_substring_semantics` (`file='Service'` against the same fixture returns all 3 — substring back-compat guard, `dirAutoConverted` not set).

- **`xray_callers impactAnalysis` — bounded-collection truncation/starvation contract pinned by tests** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_bounded-impact-analysis-test-starvation-and-truncation-contract.md`). The bounded-collection cap (`max_callers_per_level * 20`, capped at 5000) guards against latency blow-up on popular method tokens, but it can silently starve test callers that appear LATER in posting order than the cap allows. No test pinned this contract before, so a future refactor could (a) drop the `impact_analysis_truncated` flag without breaking any test — turning every "no tests found" answer into a definitive false-negative — or (b) accidentally "fix" the starvation case without updating the documented degraded behavior. Pure test additions, no production code change. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/callers_tests.rs` (helper `build_impact_starvation_fixture` builds 50 prod callers + 5 test callers with xUnit `[Fact]` attributes so `is_test_method` recognises them, postings ordered prod-then-test, `method_calls` populated so `verify_call_site_target` accepts them under a `class=` filter): `test_impact_analysis_cap_sets_truncation_flag_when_collection_capped` (cap=40, asserts `impact_analysis_truncated == true`), `test_impact_analysis_bounded_collection_starves_late_test_callers` (degraded path: with cap filled by prod callers, `tests_found.is_empty()` AND truncation flag set — if this assertion later FAILS because tests surface, a fairness fix landed and the test must be updated to assert the new contract), `test_impact_analysis_with_class_filter_avoids_starvation` (recommended path: class= filter narrows via `parent_file_ids` BEFORE the cap, all 5 test callers visible AND truncation flag clear). The actual fairness fix (separate test-caller budget or second pass over remaining postings) is intentionally out of scope of this story and tracked separately.




### Bug Fixes (edit-correctness bundle 2026-04-24)

- **`xray_edit` — `expectedContext` validates the *targeted* `occurrence`, not always the first match** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_flex-expected-context-occurrence-safety-gap.md`). Pre-fix, `apply_literal_replace` ran `check_expected_context(result, search_result.positions[0], first_len, ctx_text)` unconditionally — even when the user explicitly passed `occurrence: 2` to target the second match with disambiguating context. Two failure modes: (a) caller's intended replacement at occurrence N would be REJECTED by the gate failing on occurrence 1's surroundings (false-negative, "expected context not found" with the wrong line number); (b) symmetric false-positive — caller targeting `occurrence: 2` with WRONG context (matching occurrence 1) would silently PASS the gate and replace the second match anyway, since the gate never looked at the targeted match. **Fix**: derive `target_idx` from `edit.occurrence` (`0 → 0` for replace-all preserves historical first-match contract; `n → n-1` for 1-indexed nth-match; out-of-range clamps to 0 so the canonical "found only N time(s)" error fires below). Use `flex_match_lens[target_idx]` when present, otherwise `match_len`. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/edit_tests.rs`: `test_expected_context_validates_targeted_occurrence_not_first` (occurrence 2 + 2nd-match context succeeds, only 2nd `Foo` replaced), `test_expected_context_rejects_targeted_occurrence_with_wrong_context` (occurrence 2 + 1st-match context rejected, file unchanged), `test_expected_context_occurrence_zero_replace_all_uses_first_match_context` (back-compat guard for replace-all). Test bodies use >5 lines between the two matches because `check_expected_context` searches a ±5-line window — same-window matches can't be disambiguated and aren't the bug being fixed.

- **`xray_edit` multi-file — per-file `contentIndexUpdated` mirrors actual batch outcome instead of "always true"** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_sync-reindex-multifile-poisoned-lock-response-integrity.md`). Pre-fix, `handle_multi_file_edit`'s response-build loop set `file_result["contentIndexUpdated"] = json!(true)` UNCONDITIONALLY for every non-skipped file. When `reindex_paths_sync` returned `content_lock_poisoned = true` and `content_updated = 0`, the batch-level `summary.reindexWarning` correctly told the caller "the index lock was poisoned, FS watcher will reconcile within 500 ms" — but the per-file `contentIndexUpdated: true` told the opposite. Caller-side staleness checks (e.g. an immediate follow-up `xray_grep` looking for the just-edited symbol) trust per-file telemetry over batch warnings, so the warning was effectively dead. The single-file path already derives this from `stats.content_updated > 0` — multi-file diverged. **Fix**: mirror the single-file derivation: `contentIndexUpdated = batch_stats.as_ref().is_some_and(|s| s.content_updated > 0)`. `defIndexUpdated` and `fileListInvalidated` were already correctly derived. **Tests** in `src/mcp/handlers/edit_tests.rs`: `test_sync_reindex_multi_file_poisoned_content_lock_reports_false` (poisons the content lock via `panic!()` inside a write guard — same recipe as `watcher_tests.rs::test_process_batch_returns_false_on_poisoned_content_lock` — then asserts every per-file `contentIndexUpdated: false` AND `summary.reindexWarning` present), `test_sync_reindex_multi_file_dry_run_omits_index_telemetry` (regression guard: `dryRun: true` must NOT emit `contentIndexUpdated`/`defIndexUpdated`/`fileListInvalidated` at all). All 2129 unit tests + 102 integration tests pass; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.


### Bug Fixes (boundary-and-line-regex-followups bundle 2026-04-24)

- **`docs/e2e/git-tests.md` — fix stale `tools/list` count in T-GIT-08** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_docs-tool-count-cleanup-missed-git-tests.md`). The previous `xray serve --git` removal pass updated the unified-startup tool-count assertion in the main e2e doc but missed the dedicated git-tests doc, which still asserted "16 tools" (the pre-merge total) for the `--definitions`-less smoke test. Test author re-running this section against the merged binary would see a "15 != 16" diff and waste cycles re-checking the binary instead of the doc. Pure docs change; corrected to "15 tools including 6 git tools" to match the actual `tools/list` payload.

- **`xray_fast` — relative `..` boundary tests for `dir=` parameter** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_fast-outside-dir-boundary-edge-cases.md`). The MAJOR-14 boundary check has a single regression test (`test_xray_fast_rejects_outside_server_dir`) covering only the absolute-outside-path shape. Adds 4 sibling tests guarding the relative-path attack surface: `test_xray_fast_rejects_relative_parent_escape` (`dir: "..\\.."` resolved against server_dir, lands outside), `test_xray_fast_rejects_normalized_outside_equivalent` (`<workspace>/sub/../../outside-xyz` — textually rooted at workspace but logically escapes), `test_xray_fast_in_workspace_relative_subdir_still_accepted` (regression guard: in-workspace relative subdir with nonexistent leaf must NOT be rejected as outside), and `test_xray_fast_relative_dotdot_resolving_inside_accepted` (`<workspace>/sub/..` resolves back to workspace, must be accepted). Pure test additions, exercising the new logical-traversal branch of `is_path_within` (see story 5 below).

- **`is_path_within` — accept in-workspace `..` paths whose leaf does not exist** (closes pt.2 of `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_logical-first-empty-root-and-dotdot-nonexistent-paths.md`; pt.1 was already shipped as LIB-013 fail-closed). Pre-fix, equivalent in-workspace paths produced different verdicts only because of how they were written: `nonexistent/dir` was accepted via the no-traversal logical branch, but `src/../nonexistent/dir` was rejected — the `has_traversal=true` flag forced the canonical-fallback branch, which fails on the missing leaf. Added new helper `resolve_dotdot_logical(path, root)` that performs purely textual `..` resolution against the root (joins with root if relative, walks `Components`, pops on `ParentDir`, returns `None` when `..` would pop past the root prefix). The `has_traversal` branch now logical-resolves first and re-checks `inside`; only falls through to canonicalize when the resolution yields a path that's still NOT textually inside root (where canonicalize is needed for symlink-aware verdicts). Genuine escapes (`../outside`, `<root>/../outside`, `<root>/sub/../../outside`) are still rejected — `resolve_dotdot_logical` returns `None` (pop past root) or a path outside `root` (fails `inside`). Symlink-escape risk is no worse than the pre-existing no-traversal logical branch, which already trusts textual containment for `WalkBuilder` parity. 2 new lib tests in `src/lib_tests.rs`: `test_is_path_within_relative_dotdot_resolving_inside_accepted`, `test_is_path_within_relative_dotdot_escape_still_rejected`. The empty-root pt.1 was independently shipped earlier (LIB-013) — its test `test_lib013_is_path_within_empty_root_refuses` is unchanged.

- **`xray_grep` — `linePatterns` array for literal-comma-safe lineRegex patterns** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_line-regex-literal-comma-separator-gap.md`). The `lineRegex=true` mode unconditionally splits `terms` on `,` to support multi-pattern OR/AND, which makes literal `,` inside a single pattern impossible to express: `terms="^ERROR,WARN:"` becomes two regexes `^ERROR` + `WARN:` instead of one match for `^ERROR,WARN: ...` log-prefix lines, and CSV-shape regexes like `^[^,]+,[^,]+$` fragment into nonsense. Added new optional schema field `linePatterns: array of strings`: each entry is taken verbatim (no comma-split, no trim, regex-significant whitespace preserved), and is only consumed by the `lineRegex=true` mode. Mutually exclusive with `terms` (passing both → error with hint that names the precise difference: `,` separator vs literal). Requires `lineRegex=true` (passing `linePatterns` without it → eager error so a typo doesn't silently fall through to substring/regex modes that ignore the array). The legacy `terms.split(',')` path is preserved for back-compat. `handle_line_regex_search` signature changed from `terms_str: &str` to `patterns: Vec<String>` — the caller (`handle_xray_grep`) chooses the source. Schema description for `lineRegex` updated to point at `linePatterns` for literal-comma cases. `KNOWN_GREP_PARAMS` is auto-discovered from the schema, so no separate validator update is needed. 6 new tests in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests_line_regex.rs`: `line_patterns_literal_comma_in_log_prefix`, `line_patterns_csv_two_columns_regex`, `line_patterns_multiple_patterns_or_semantics`, `line_patterns_and_terms_mutually_exclusive`, `line_patterns_requires_line_regex_true`, `line_patterns_terms_comma_split_back_compat`. All 2134 unit tests + 104 line-regex tests pass; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.



### Bug Fixes (diagnostic-tests bundle 2026-04-24)

- **`xray_edit` — reject wrong-type values for canonical top-level params with concrete error messages** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_edit-top-level-param-type-and-operations-path-hints.md`). The `handle_xray_edit` shape gate already had `check_unknown_top_level_params` (alias hints + Levenshtein nearest-match), but the canonical params themselves were parsed via `args.get("key").and_then(|v| v.as_str() / .as_bool() / .as_u64())` — so a caller passing the right key with the wrong JSON type (`path: 123`, `paths: "a.txt"`, `regex: "true"`, `dryRun: 1`, `expectedLineCount: "10"`, `operations: { ... }`) silently fell through to None / default-false and surfaced misleading downstream errors (`"Missing required parameter: 'path'"`, `"Specify 'operations' or 'edits'"`, count mismatch with stale literal). New helper `check_top_level_param_types` runs immediately after the unknown-key check (so a typo'd key still gets the alias hint, not a generic type error) and validates each canonical key against its expected JSON shape, including per-element type-check for `paths[]` items. Error format mirrors the Mode B `expect_*_field` diagnostics: `"Parameter 'path' must be a string, got number."` / `"Parameter 'paths[1]' must be a string, got number."`. Also adds a symmetric `test_missing_path_detects_nested_path_in_operations` test — the existing `missing_path_error_message` already detected nested-`path` inside `operations[]` via `KNOWN_EDIT_OBJECT_FIELDS` (which covers Mode A `startLine`/`endLine`/`content`), but only the `_in_edits` variant had test coverage. 8 new unit tests in `src/mcp/handlers/edit_tests.rs`. All 2124 unit tests + 102 line-regex tests pass; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.

- **`xray_grep` — fill missing tie-break / line-level pruning regression tests** (closes follow-ups `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_phrase-tier-a-parallel-order-and-concurrency-guards.md` and `..._phrase-tier-b-pruning-and-tiebreak-test-gaps.md`). The deterministic tie-break (`b.lines.len().cmp(&a.lines.len()).then_with(|| a.file_path.cmp(&b.file_path))`) ships in all three handlers (`handle_phrase_search`, `handle_multi_phrase_search`, `handle_line_regex_search`) since the Tier-B perf work, but only the single-phrase variant had a regression test — the multi-phrase and lineRegex paths could silently regress if a refactor dropped the secondary key. Tier-B line-level posting intersection (`intersect_sorted_unique`) was unit-tested in isolation but no test exercised the full handler path that proves files with phrase tokens on DIFFERENT lines are pruned out. 3 new tests in `src/mcp/handlers/handlers_tests_grep.rs`: `test_xray_grep_multi_phrase_sort_tie_break_by_path` (6 equal-occurrence files, threads=4, asserts ascending paths AND identical order across 5 repeated `phrase-or` runs), `test_xray_grep_line_regex_sort_tie_break_by_path` (same shape with `lineRegex: true` + `regex: true` + `^public class` pattern), and `test_xray_grep_phrase_line_level_pruning_same_line_vs_split_lines` (matching.cs with both phrase tokens on one line → included; split.cs with tokens on different lines but file-level intersection passes → must be pruned out; unrelated.cs with the literal phrase → included). Pure test additions, no production code change. All 2124 unit tests + 102 line-regex tests pass; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.


### Bug Fixes (serve-path follow-up 2026-04-24)


- **`xray serve` — honour persisted `respect_git_exclude` for watcher / periodic rescan / MCP reindex paths** (closes `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_respect-git-exclude-serve-persisted-semantics.md`, follow-up to the Bug 4 entry below). The 2026-04-23 fix correctly persisted `respect_git_exclude` on disk and reused it in `cmd_fast` / `load_grep_index` via [`resolve_respect_git_exclude()`](src/cli/mod.rs:421). It MISSED `cmd_serve`: `args.respect_git_exclude` (raw CLI value) flowed straight into `HandlerContext.respect_git_exclude`, `start_watcher`, `start_periodic_rescan`, and the workspace-switch / MCP `xray_reindex*` paths that read from `ctx.respect_git_exclude`. Symptom: a user who built indexes once with `--respect-git-exclude` and then restarted `xray serve` WITHOUT the flag would see correct startup state (the loaded index still excluded the right files) but the very first reconcile (`xray_reindex`, watcher batch on a new file, periodic rescan, workspace-switch rebuild) would silently re-walk with `git_exclude(false)` and re-add `.git/info/exclude` files — a delayed, easy-to-miss data leak that looked exactly like the previous Bug 4. **Fix**: `load_or_build_content_index` and `load_or_build_definition_index` in `src/cli/serve.rs` now return `(index, effective_respect_git_exclude)` — the second element is the result of `super::resolve_respect_git_exclude("serve/content" | "serve/definitions", Some(loaded.respect_git_exclude), cli_flag)` when an existing index loads from disk (preserving the persisted opt-in with a stderr warning on CLI mismatch), or the raw CLI flag on cold start. `cmd_serve` then OR-merges the two effective values (stricter `true` wins so excluded files cannot leak through the walker even in the exotic case of mixed content/def persisted state — with a warn log naming both values) and threads the merged value into `start_watcher`, `start_periodic_rescan`, and `HandlerContext.respect_git_exclude`. Downstream MCP rebuild call-sites in `mcp/handlers/mod.rs` (`xray_reindex`, `xray_reindex_definitions`, `restart_watcher_for_workspace`, content/def background fallback) and `mcp/handlers/fast.rs` (auto-rebuild) already read from `ctx.respect_git_exclude` — no per-call-site edit needed. `resolve_respect_git_exclude` was promoted from `fn` to `pub(crate) fn` so the `super::serve` module can reuse it. **Out of scope**: `determine_initial_binding` still receives the raw CLI flag (it is a yes/no "are there source files" probe; an over-/under-count by a few excluded files never flips Resolved ↔ Unresolved). **Tests** (`src/cli/serve.rs::serve_respect_git_exclude_tests`): `serve_load_preserves_persisted_respect_git_exclude_for_content_index` (build with flag=true, save, load with CLI=false, assert effective=true), `serve_load_preserves_persisted_respect_git_exclude_for_definition_index` (cfg lang-csharp, same shape), `serve_cold_start_uses_cli_flag_when_no_persisted_index` (no persisted state, CLI flag passes through). All 12 `respect_git_exclude` tests pass; `cargo check --tests` clean.


### Features

- **Advisory hints for `xray_callers` and `xray_definitions` — surface known AST blind spots so the LLM agent cross-checks before drawing conclusions** (closes `user-stories/xray-response-hints-for-incomplete-results.md`; promoted from real session post-mortem 2026-04-23 where an agent silently built conclusions on an incomplete `xray_callers` result because `class=Foo` filter excluded DI-injected `IFoo` interface call sites). Three new shape-based hints, all in the new `src/mcp/handlers/advisory_hints.rs` module:
  1. **`xray_callers` interface-vias caveat** — when `class=Foo` is passed and the indexed `Foo` declares one or more interface base types (looked up via `name_index` + `kind == Interface`), the response now includes an `advisories[]` entry naming every detected interface and suggesting `class=IFoo` (or no `class=`) to include interface-receiver call sites. Generic suffixes are stripped (`IRepository<T>` → `IRepository`) before lookup. Skips false positives where the base type is a class, not an interface.
  2. **`xray_callers` low-count cross-check hint** — when `1..=3` callers are returned **AND the result was not truncated**, the response includes an advisory naming the asymmetry between AST-aware `xray_callers` (which honours receiver type and may miss DI-injected, dynamic-dispatch, or hard-to-infer-`var` call sites) and text-only `xray_grep`, with a copy-pasteable `xray_grep terms='MethodName' countOnly=true` command to validate completeness. Threshold deliberately excludes `0` (covered by the existing nearest-match `hint`) and `>3` (where the cost-benefit of cross-check flips). **Truncation guard**: the hint is suppressed when `summary.truncated` (hit `maxTotalNodes` cap) or `summary.perLevelTruncated` (hit `maxCallersPerLevel` cap) is set — otherwise a method with 5 real callers capped at `maxCallersPerLevel=2` would falsely emit "Found 2 callers…" and mis-attribute the cap to AST blind spots. Wired identically in both single-method and multi-method (batch comma-separated) paths; regression tests `test_advisory_low_count_suppressed_when_truncated` and `test_advisory_low_count_emitted_in_multi_method_batch` guard against single/multi drift.
  3. **`xray_definitions` value-source hint** — Property/Field whose `attributes[]` contain at least one double-quoted string literal now emits a `valueSourceHint` field with the extracted literals as ready-to-grep keys and a `xray_grep terms='key1,key2' ext='xml,json,config,yaml,manifestxml'` command. **Shape-based heuristic, deliberately broad**: detection requires only (a) `kind == Property | Field` and (b) at least one extractable string literal across the attribute set — ALL string literals from ALL attributes are surfaced as grep keys (not just the "first argument" of the first attribute), and there is no body/initializer check (the index does not store body for Property/Field). The framing `"If any attribute binds to external configuration..."` keeps the hint honest for non-binder attributes like `[Display("Name")]` — it never claims the attribute IS a binder, only suggests where to look IF it is. **No hardcoded attribute name list** (deliberately rejected during design — every team has custom binders like `[Knob]`, `[FromManifest]`, `[Tenanted]`, and any allow-list goes stale). Catches `[ConfigurationProperty(...)]`, `[FromKeyVault(...)]`, `[AppSetting(...)]`, `@Value("${...}")`, `#[serde(rename = "...")]` and equivalents in any framework / language with no per-framework code.

  All three are pure helpers (no I/O, no allocation outside the hint string) with 27 unit tests in `advisory_hints::tests` covering positive cases, negative cases, and edge conditions (empty literals, escaped quotes, unterminated literals, generic-suffix stripping, base-class-not-interface, threshold boundaries 0/1/3/4, plural/singular). 5 integration tests in `callers_tests.rs` exercise the wiring end-to-end through `handle_xray_callers` (single-method positive + interface-vias positive/negative + truncation suppression + multi-method batch). Tool descriptions for `xray_callers` and `xray_definitions` in `tool_definitions()` document the new `advisories[]` and `valueSourceHint` response fields so MCP clients see them at schema-discovery time, not just from runtime probing. The hints follow the principle "xray is an observation-divider, not a classifier" — they always frame as "if X, then try Y", never claim "X is true".



- **`xray_git_history` deleted-file cold path — drop redundant existence probe** (closes Bug 7 of `docs/bug-reports/2026-04-23_consolidated-fix-plan.md`). `file_history` in `src/git/mod.rs` previously made up to **3 git-spawn round-trips** for a single deleted-file query: `git log --follow` (returns 0) → `file_ever_existed_in_git` (extra `git log --all --max-count=1`) → `git log` (no-follow). The middle existence-probe spawn is redundant: when `--follow` returns 0, the no-follow retry itself returns the same correctness signal (>0 → file existed and was deleted; 0 → file genuinely never existed or no commits in active filter). Removed the gate; spawn count for the deleted-file cold path drops from 3 → 2 (~50–100 ms saved on big repos per query). Never-existed and exists-with-commits paths are unchanged in spawn count. `file_ever_existed_in_git` itself is kept — other call sites (`repo_activity`, `annotate_empty_git_result` in `handle_git_history` / `handle_git_authors` / `handle_git_activity`) still need an explicit "existed?" boolean for warning generation. Existing regression tests `test_file_history_returns_commits_for_deleted_file` and `test_file_history_returns_empty_for_never_existed_file` cover both branches with the new flow.



### Bug Fixes (hardening bundle 2026-04-23)

- **`xray_edit` Mode A — empty file now means 0 addressable lines, REPLACE/DELETE rejected with INSERT hint** (closes follow-up `docs/user-stories/todo_approved_2026-04-24_expected-line-count-empty-file-semantics.md`, surfaced during review of the `expectedLineCount` Mode B fix below). After that fix `count_lines("") == 0` (human/editor semantics, surfaced as `originalLineCount` / `newLineCount`), but `apply_line_operations` still computed `line_count = lines.len()` from `normalized.split('\n').collect()` — for an empty file `""` that yields `[""]`, so `line_count` was silently `1`. Two contracts on one value: `expectedLineCount: 0` AND `REPLACE 1..1` both succeeded on an empty file (the latter writing content with no trailing `\n`, while the response simultaneously reported `originalLineCount: 0`). The carve-out is one line in `apply_line_operations`: `let line_count = if lines == [""] { 0 } else { lines.len() };` — empty-file detection is exact (`[""]` is the unique split-output for `""`), non-empty files are unchanged. REPLACE/DELETE on a 0-line file now returns `"Cannot replace/delete lines in empty file (0 lines). To write content into an empty (or auto-created) file, use INSERT mode: startLine: 1, endLine: 0, content: '...'"` — the canonical INSERT idiom is spelled out so the LLM does not retry with a guessed range. INSERT (`startLine: 1, endLine: 0`) is unaffected — it was already correct and remains the auto-create / write-into-empty path. 3 new regression tests in `edit_tests.rs`: `test_empty_file_replace_rejected_with_insert_hint` (the new error path + spelled-out hint), `test_empty_file_insert_with_expected_line_count_zero` (empty + `expectedLineCount: 0` + INSERT happy path), `test_round_trip_new_line_count_to_expected_line_count` (edit a file ending in `\n`, read `newLineCount` from the response, feed back as `expectedLineCount` on the next edit — guards against the historical `split('\n').count()` off-by-one). One existing test comment (`test_auto_create_mode_a_replace_on_nonexistent_fails`) corrected — it previously said "treated as 1-line empty file", now says "treated as empty / 0 lines". Tool-schema `operations` description in `tips.rs` updated with one line: "EMPTY FILE (incl. auto-created / nonexistent) = 0 lines: REPLACE/DELETE error with hint; only INSERT (startLine: 1, endLine: 0) is valid". All 2099 unit tests pass; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.

- **`xray_edit` — `expectedLineCount` now honored in Mode B (search/replace), and counts lines the way humans/editors/`xray_definitions` do** (reported by an external test report at `C:/Projects/MainApp/xray-test-report_2026-04-23.md`, §1.12 "Bug detail"). Two coupled fixes in `src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs::apply_edits_to_content`. (1) **Mode B was silently ignoring `expectedLineCount`**: the safety check lived inside the `EditMode::Operations` (Mode A) match arm only, so a Mode B (text-match) edit with `expectedLineCount: 99999` against a 391-line file applied the edit anyway instead of aborting. The check is now lifted ABOVE the `match mode`, so it runs once for both modes. (2) **Off-by-one for files ending in `\n`**: the previous Mode A check used `normalized.split('\n').count()`, which for a typical file `"a\nb\nc\n"` returns 4 (the empty element after the final terminator) — but no read tool ever surfaces that "phantom" line: `xray_definitions` / `xray_grep` / editors all use 1-based line numbers where the trailing `\n` is a terminator, not a line. So an LLM that read `endLine: 391` from `xray_definitions` and then passed `expectedLineCount: 391` got `Expected 391 lines, file has 392`. New `count_lines(s) -> usize` helper (`""` → 0; `"a"` / `"a\n"` → 1; `"a\nb"` / `"a\nb\n"` → 2) is now used for both the `expectedLineCount` comparison AND for the `original_line_count` / `new_line_count` fields surfaced in the response — so the caller can round-trip `response.newLineCount` back into the next edit's `expectedLineCount` without an off-by-one. Mode A line-range op semantics are unchanged (`apply_line_operations` still uses `lines.len()` from `split('\n')` internally for the `endLine ≤ N` range check; the addressable `1..=N` content range was always human-aligned, only the unreachable `N+1` "phantom" slot existed). 4 new unit tests in `src/mcp/handlers/edit_tests.rs` (`test_mode_b_expected_line_count_mismatch` — the regression for the report's exact scenario; `test_mode_b_expected_line_count_match` — happy path; `test_expected_line_count_human_semantics` — pins the count convention) plus an updated `test_mode_a_expected_line_count_match` (`expectedLineCount: 4 → 3` for `"a\nb\nc\n"`). Tool-schema description (`src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs`) and `tips.rs` updated to spell out the convention and the round-trip property. All 2064 unit tests pass; `cargo clippy --bin xray --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.

- **`xray_definitions` on huge XML files — explicit 64 MiB guard before in-memory parse** (closes Bug 6 of `docs/bug-reports/2026-04-23_consolidated-fix-plan.md`). `handle_xray_definitions` for the on-demand XML path called `std::fs::read_to_string(file_path)` without an upper bound, so a multi-gigabyte XML file (cf. test fixtures, log dumps, dataset exports) would attempt to allocate the whole file into a `String` and OOM the MCP server process. The fix adds `MAX_XML_BYTES = 64 * 1024 * 1024` and a `metadata().len()` pre-check that returns a structured error message (`"XML file '{}' is {} bytes, which exceeds the max supported size of {} bytes (64 MiB). xray_definitions parses the whole file in-memory; use xray_grep for line-level search over very large files."`) BEFORE allocation. Regression test `test_xml_on_demand_rejects_files_above_max_size` in `definitions_tests.rs` uses `File::set_len(65 MiB)` (sparse file — costs zero disk) to assert the guard fires with the documented message.

- **`xray_grep` phrase-verification thread panic — surface to caller via `tracing::warn`** (closes Bug 9). `collect_phrase_matches` ran phrase verification across `thread::scope`d worker threads and silently dropped panics with `if let Ok(local) = h.join() { all.extend(local); }`. A panicking worker (regex misuse, downstream IO, allocator failure under memory pressure) reduced the result set without any warning — the caller saw "fewer matches than expected" with no diagnostic. The join loop now match-arms `Err(_)` to a `worker_panics` counter and emits `tracing::warn!(worker_panics, "phrase verification worker(s) panicked; result set may be incomplete")` once after the loop. The result set still returns (best-effort) — the change is a visibility fix only, not a behaviour change.

- **`xray_edit` rename durability on Unix — fsync the parent directory** (closes Bug 1). After `rename_replace(&tmp, resolved)` succeeds in the multi-file write loop, on Unix the rename is only durable across power loss / hard-kill once the parent directory's metadata is fsync'd (POSIX rename atomicity guarantees in-tree visibility, NOT post-crash recovery — the directory entry update lives in the parent inode). Added a best-effort `#[cfg(unix)] { if let Some(parent) = resolved.parent() && let Ok(dir) = std::fs::File::open(parent) { let _ = dir.sync_all(); } }` block. Errors from the open/sync are swallowed — this is a hardening pass, not a correctness gate; on filesystems where parent fsync is a no-op (e.g. certain tmpfs configurations) the call costs ~0. Windows path is unchanged (`MoveFileEx` already provides crash-consistent rename when the target lives on the same volume).

- **`xray_definitions` / workspace-switch — case-sensitive path comparison on Unix** (closes Bug 8). Three sites compared file paths via `eq_ignore_ascii_case` (`src/mcp/server.rs:82` and `src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs` lines 1582 + 1749 — both copies of the workspace-switch detection in `handle_xray_reindex_inner` and the secondary content-only handler). On case-sensitive filesystems (Linux, macOS in case-sensitive HFS+ / APFS configurations) `/repos/Xray` and `/repos/xray` are TWO DIFFERENT directories, so the comparison incorrectly classified a real workspace switch as "same dir" and skipped the rebuild + watcher restart + cache invalidation cascade. Replaced with `code_xray::path_eq(&a, &b)` (cfg(windows) ASCII-fold, cfg(not(windows)) byte-compare). The existing `test_path_eq_case_sensitive_on_unix` in `lib_tests.rs` is the regression guard — the production sites are now correct by construction (single `path_eq` helper, no per-site `eq_ignore_ascii_case` reintroduction). One unrelated `eq_ignore_ascii_case` in `src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs:682` is intentionally KEPT — it folds **file extensions** (`.cs` vs `.CS`), not file paths.

- **`docs/e2e/mcp-definitions-tests.md` — fix stale param name `onDemand` → `xmlOnDemand`** (closes Bug 5). Three test cases (lines 463 / 469 / 497) cited the legacy parameter name `onDemand: true`. The runtime parameter has been `xmlOnDemand` since the cleanup, so any e2e harness following the doc literally would silently drop the flag (Bug 5 of `docs/bug-reports/2026-04-23_consolidated-fix-plan.md`). Doc-only change.



### Bug Fixes
- **`--respect-git-exclude` end-to-end (real this time)** — Closes Bug 4 from `docs/bug-reports/2026-04-23_consolidated-fix-plan.md`. PR #128 plumbed the flag into `HandlerContext` and the two CLI args structs, but five walker construction sites in the watcher / incremental / definitions builders were still hardcoded to `git_exclude(false)`. After the initial build, any reconcile (`xray_reindex`, `xray_reindex_definitions`, watcher batch, periodic rescan, `cross_load_definition_index`, `start_periodic_rescan`, `restart_watcher_for_workspace`, `load_or_build_definition_index`) silently re-walked excluded files and re-added them — a real data leak vs. the explicit user opt-in. **Walker sites fixed**: `src/definitions/mod.rs::collect_source_files`, `src/definitions/incremental.rs::reconcile_definition_index` (test) + `reconcile_definition_index_nonblocking`, `src/mcp/watcher.rs::scan_dir_state`, `src/mcp/handlers/mod.rs::has_source_files`. The flag is now threaded through every walker construction via function params (no globals). **Persistence (closes Bug 2)**: the value is now stored on `FileIndex`, `ContentIndex`, and `DefinitionIndex` (`#[serde(default)]` for backward read of older indexes) and round-trips through bincode + the `*.meta` header. `FILE_INDEX_VERSION` 1→2, `CONTENT_INDEX_VERSION` 2→3, `DEFINITION_INDEX_VERSION` 2→3 — stale indexes auto-rebuild as before. New helper `resolve_respect_git_exclude(index_kind, persisted, cli_flag)` in `src/cli/mod.rs` is used by both `cmd_fast` and `load_grep_index` stale-rebuild paths to PREFER the persisted value over the CLI flag (with a stderr warning on mismatch), so a user who originally built with `--respect-git-exclude` does not silently lose their setting on auto-rebuild. **`DefIndexArgs` (clap)** gained `--respect-git-exclude` so the standalone `xray index-definitions` honours the flag like `xray index` / `xray index-content` already did. **Tests (closes Bug 3)**: 5 new integration tests in `src/main_tests.rs` exercise the full path against a real `git init` + `.git/info/exclude` repo: `build_index_respects_git_info_exclude`, `build_content_index_respects_git_info_exclude`, `build_definition_index_respects_git_info_exclude` (cfg lang-csharp), `incremental_reconcile_respects_git_info_exclude` (cfg lang-csharp — reproduces the original bug: builds with the flag, drops a new excluded file on disk, calls `reconcile_definition_index`, asserts the excluded class is NOT picked up), `auto_rebuild_preserves_persisted_respect_git_exclude` (saves a content index with the flag, reloads via `load_content_index`, asserts the field round-trips and excluded tokens stay absent). `cargo check --tests --features lang-csharp` clean. ~26 production / test call-sites threaded the new bool; field-count guard tests for `FileIndex` / `ContentIndex` / `DefinitionIndex` updated. The existing PR #128 CHANGELOG entry has been amended with an "Update 2026-04-23" note pointing here so the over-claim of "end-to-end" doesn't read as misleading.

### Removed
- **`xray_edit` `find_with_retry` cleanup-magic — removed silent Step 2 (strip-trailing-whitespace) and Step 3 (trim-blank-lines) retries** (approved-todo: `docs/todo_approved_2026-04-23_xray-edit-cleanup-magic.md`, PR #1). Both retries silently rewrote the search text and matched a similar-looking block, masking semantic mismatches and leading callers (especially LLM agents) to write the wrong bytes — the top transcript-driven cause of `xray_edit → built-in replace_string_in_file` policy violations. The cascade is now exact-match + opt-in flex-whitespace (Step 4 — unchanged, gated by `expectedContext`). The two helpers `strip_trailing_whitespace_per_line` and `trim_blank_lines` are deleted (verified zero callers remain). Whitespace and blank-line drift now surface as `Text not found` errors with a categorised `Nearest match` hint (see Added below). **Backward compatibility**: callers that relied on the silent retries receive `Text not found` instead of a soft warning. This is intentional — those are the silent-misfire cases the change targets. 5 affected `edit_tests.rs` tests inverted to assert the new diagnose-first behaviour (`test_no_silent_match_*`); 2 helper unit tests deleted along with their helpers.

### Changed
- **`xray_edit` nearest-match byte-diff hint threshold lowered from 0.99 → 0.80** (`NEAREST_MATCH_BYTE_DIFF_THRESHOLD`). After Step 2/3 removal, multi-line whitespace / blank-line drift drops nearest-match similarity into the 0.80–0.95 band — right when the byte-level hint is most needed. The old 0.99 threshold suppressed it for exactly those cases. Implementation lives next to the existing `NEAREST_MATCH_MIN_SIMILARITY` const in `src/mcp/handlers/edit.rs`.
- **`xray_edit` tool description for `paths`** (`src/tips.rs`) replaces the false claim "Transactional: if any file fails, none are written" with the honest "Transactional on input validation, content edits, and per-file write … in the rare event a rename fails mid-batch, earlier files in the batch may remain committed and are listed in the error response (use `git restore` to roll back)". Documents the actual Phase 3b semantics (per-file temp+rename with backup-swap on Windows; no batch-wide rollback yet).

### Added
- **`xray_edit` `detect_diff_category` — categorised hint appended to `Nearest match`** (PR #1). Classifies the difference between the search text and its nearest match into one of four categories: `crlfVsLf` (line-ending normalisation would make them equal), `leadingOrTrailingBlankLines` (surrounding `\n` padding differs), `trailingWhitespace` (only trailing spaces/tabs per line differ), `unicodeConfusable` (only NBSP, en/em-dash, or smart quotes differ). The detector is conservative — any byte difference outside the relevant equivalence class disqualifies the category. Format: `". First difference at byte N: search has X, file has Y (category: trailingWhitespace)"`. 5 new unit tests cover each category + the no-recognised-pattern case.
- **`xray_edit` Mode A INSERT out-of-range — positive append-idiom hint** (closes Issue 1 from `docs/user-stories/xray-edit-ux-improvements.md` and `docs/user-stories/xray-edit-ux-issues-2026-04-21.md`). When `apply_line_operations` rejects an INSERT op (`endLine < startLine`) with `startLine > line_count + 1`, the error now spells out the exact append idiom: `… To append to end of file, pass startLine: N+1, endLine: N (INSERT mode at line N+1)`. Closes the recurring trap where agents tried `startLine: "end"` or guessed off-by-one coordinates. ~5 LOC + 1 unit test (`test_insert_out_of_range_includes_append_hint`).
- **`xray_edit` multi-file Phase 3b error — `committedFiles: […]` payload** (PR #1, item 1.5). When a rename fails partway through a multi-file batch, the error message now appends a JSON array of the file paths that already committed (renames succeeded for indices `0..renamed`). These cannot be rolled back by the tool — `git restore` is the recovery path — and the explicit list lets the caller act without re-deriving it from the diff response.

### Bug Fixes
- **`xray_grep` multi-term substring — auto-balance dominant common terms so rare-term matches stay visible** (validation reformulation of `docs/todo_approved_2026-04-23_xray-grep-edit-followups.md` original story #3 — the report "`localStorage` (1953 matches) drowned out `TODO` (50 matches) in a single multi-term query"). Pure per-term occurrence cap was rejected as too blunt; the shipped design only fires when there's a real imbalance and only trims the long tail of dominant-only files. **Trigger**: multi-term substring-OR query (mode='or' or default; AND mode is unaffected because it already requires every term to match per file) where one term contributes ≥10× more total occurrences than the rarest matched term, computed from the FULL result set BEFORE `maxResults` truncation. **Trim policy**: among files where the dominant term is the ONLY matched term, keep the top `cap` by `tf_idf` (so the strongest dominant hits survive) and drop the rest. Files matched by ≥2 distinct terms are NEVER dropped — cross-term relevance is the high-signal case. **Cap derivation**: explicit `maxOccurrencesPerTerm=N` (0..=10000) wins; otherwise `min(100, max(20, 2 * second_max))` — small enough to keep the response focused, large enough that the dominant term's strongest hits surface. **New params**: `autoBalance: bool` (default `true`, opt-out via `false`), `maxOccurrencesPerTerm: u64` (default `0` = derive). Both validated by the new schema-derived `arg_validation::check_unknown_args` (added in the entry above) so typos like `autobalance` get a `Did you mean 'autoBalance'?` hint. **Response surface**: when balancing fires, `summary.autoBalance` carries `{ dominantTerm, dominantOccurrences, secondMaxOccurrences, minNonzeroOccurrences, ratio, cap, droppedFiles, hint }`, and the human-readable hint is also appended to `summary.warnings[]` so warning-aware clients see it without checking a new field. The hint names the dominant term, the ratio, the dropped count, the cap, and both opt-outs (`autoBalance=false` / `maxOccurrencesPerTerm=N`). **Implementation surface**: `FileScoreEntry` gained `per_term_occurrences: Vec<usize>` (lazily grown during `score_token_postings`; tracked per `term_idx` so post-aggregation balancing has the data it needs without re-running the inverted-index lookup). New `apply_auto_balance(results, term_count, raw_terms, user_cap) -> Option<AutoBalanceInfo>` lives at the top of `src/mcp/handlers/grep.rs` next to the other shared helpers; called from `handle_substring_search` after `finalize_grep_results` and BEFORE `max_results.truncate` so the cap operates on the full result set. New `inject_auto_balance(summary, info)` writes the structured field plus the warning string. **Scope**: only substring mode (the most common multi-term path; `localStorage`/`TODO`-style keyword queries). Phrase / regex / lineRegex paths are unchanged — their result aggregation is per-line not per-term, so the imbalance signal is not directly available, and the `tf_idf`-based ranking already handles the imbalance differently. **Tests**: 6 unit tests in `src/mcp/handlers/grep_tests_additional.rs` covering trigger (1 rare + 100 dominant-only, ratio=20×, cap=20, drops 80), single-term skip, ratio-below-threshold (9×) skip, explicit `maxOccurrencesPerTerm` override (cap=5 wins over derived cap=20), multi-term files always kept (50 dom-only + 1 both-terms with cap=10 → 1 multi + 10 dom kept), and no-op when no dominant-only files exist. All 2033 unit tests pass; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. **Backward compatibility**: opt-out via `autoBalance=false` returns the previous TF-IDF order verbatim; `summary.autoBalance` is omitted entirely when balancing did not fire (no schema churn for callers who don't query the field). Closes story NEW-#2 in the validation document.

- **All MCP tools — silent-ignore of unknown args replaced with actionable warnings + opt-in strict mode** (validation of `docs/todo_approved_2026-04-23_xray-grep-edit-followups.md` exposed the systemic root cause behind multiple agent-side complaints: "`includePattern` doesn't filter", "`isRegexp: true` returns invalid input", "alien arg crashed nothing but search ran over the whole repo"). Every handler parsed args via `args.get("key").and_then(...)` (131 occurrences across 7 handler files), so any misspelled or alien-named key (`includePattern`, `isRegexp`, `excludePattern`, `query`, `path`, `since`, ...) was silently dropped — the tool ran with the agent's intended filter missing, returning surprising results that looked like xray bugs. New `src/mcp/handlers/arg_validation.rs` (~285 LOC, 19 unit tests) extracts the canonical allowed-args set per tool from `tool_definitions(&[]).input_schema.properties` (single source of truth, no per-handler hardcoding) and runs `check_unknown_args` in `dispatch_tool` BEFORE the handler runs. Two layers of feedback: (1) **alias table** (~30 entries) maps the most common LLM/agent mistakes to direct hints — `isRegexp→regex`, `includePattern→file` (with `+ note: 'substring + comma-OR, not glob'`), `excludePattern→excludeDir`, `glob→pattern`, `query→terms`, `limit→maxResults`, `function→method`, `caller/callee→direction='up'/'down'`, `preview→dryRun`, `find/oldText/newText→edits`, `since/until→from/to`, `repository/repoPath→repo`, `path→file`, `directory→dir`, `filePath/file_path→file`. (2) **Jaro-Winkler nearest-match fallback** (`name_similarity`, threshold 0.80) for typos not in the table — e.g. `maxResult` (missing `s`) gets `Did you mean 'maxResults'? (similarity 95%)`. **Default behavior**: warning is injected as `summary.unknownArgsWarning` + structured `summary.unknownArgs[]` so the tool keeps running (no breaking change for existing callers / scripts that may pass extra metadata). **Strict mode** (opt-in via `XRAY_STRICT_ARGS=1`/`true`/`yes`/`on`): hard-errors with `error: "UNKNOWN_ARGS"` + per-key hints + `envHint` instructing how to disable — intended for CI gates and agent test runners that want to surface the mistake immediately. Strict-mode env var is read fresh per call (no global state cached).
